% natural title->abstract->cluster preview reading order. Cluster preview
% page 2 inserted between abstract and Introduction.
\begin{abstract}
A zero-fitted-exponent ladder $\beta=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ reproduces every indicator of the Bettencourt 2007 22-panel within its 95\,\% confidence interval. Here $\beta$ is the urban scaling exponent. The relay-depth $H$ is the hierarchy of coordination layers in the city's productive system without using observed $\beta$. The framework is falsified if any indicator falls outside its CI under the zero-fitted-exponent assignment.
\end{abstract}

% V66: Hero equation tcolorbox + Bettencourt 22 main figure on page 1

% V226: 数式ボックス上 margin -0.5cm 追加圧縮 (= -0.5cm -> -1.0cm)、 author footer page 1 収束 trigger
% =====================================================================
\vspace*{-1.0cm}
\begingroup
\singlespacing
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=black!5!white, colframe=black!50!white, boxrule=0.6pt, arc=2pt, left=10pt, right=10pt, top=6pt, bottom=6pt]
\centering
\(\displaystyle
\beta \;=\; 1 \;\pm\; \frac{1}{H \ln(2H+1)}
\)

\vspace{0.3em}
\begin{flushleft}\small
\textbullet\; \(\beta\) = urban scaling exponent: a city \(N\) times larger has, for the given indicator, approximately \(N^{\beta}\) times the value (cross-city comparison, not annual growth). \\
\textbullet\; \(H\) = relay-depth (hierarchy of coordination layers in the city's productive system). \\
\textbullet\; Branch sign (\(\pm\)) = fixed ex-ante from network type + substrate constraint, not fitted.
\end{flushleft}
\end{tcolorbox}
\vspace{-0.3em}
{\centering\small\itshape All 22 Bettencourt indicators within 95\,\% CI \quad{\normalfont\textbullet}\quad Zero fitted exponents \quad{\normalfont\textbullet}\quad Falsified if direct-strict drops below $11/22$\par}

\vspace{0.5em}
\par\nobreak\vspace{0.3em}\nopagebreak

\nopagebreak\noindent\centerline{\includegraphics[width=0.75\linewidth, height=7.3cm, keepaspectratio=false, trim=0pt 0pt 100pt 0pt, clip]{paper4_fig_main.png}}\nopagebreak

\nopagebreak\noindent{\small\textbf{Figure 1: Bettencourt 22-indicator closure.} Forest plot of all 22 indicators (95\,\% CI) vs the zero-fitted-exponent ladder \(\beta = 1 \pm 1/[H \ln(2H+1)]\). The relay-depth \(H \in \{1,\dots,8\}\) is the hierarchy of coordination layers; both \(H\) and the branch sign (\(\pm\)) are derived structurally from network type and substrate constraint, not by fitting. See SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins} for full provenance.\par}
\refstepcounter{figure}\label{fig:bettencourt_22_closure}

\begin{tabular}{>{\centering\arraybackslash}m{1.6cm}m{0.42\linewidth}m{0.47\linewidth}}

\specialrule{1.5pt}{0pt}{0pt}
\textbf{Paper 1} & ``Singularity abundance'' narrative is refuted: even with full integer-$H$ extrapolation through 2066, world GDP per capita grows only $+27\%$ (about 0.57\,\%/yr compounded over 42 years) from the 2024 baseline. & \textbf{First} closed-form world GDP--population law over 200 years (1820--2024, $R^2{=}0.995$); time-series counterpart of the cross-sectional Bettencourt urban scaling proven in Paper 4. \\
\specialrule{0.8pt}{0pt}{0pt}
\textbf{Paper 2} & After von Foerster: an engine of \emph{pairwise} human interaction that fits 70{,}000 years of population reaches the AGI era, recasting the von Foerster 1960 doomsday as a phase-transition node, not a literal blow-up. & \textbf{First} closed-form $dN/dt = a_0 N^2$ verification across 300{,}000 years and 85 observations (300k BCE--2025 CE; $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}{=}383$); post-1971 deviation absorbed into a slow $L_{\rm pop}(t)$ factor. \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 3} & AGI emergence --- next civilisational phase transition $H{=}6{\to}7$ --- is mathematically datable: $2031.4 \pm 2.2$ CE, not doom but a quantifiable phase shift. & \textbf{First mathematically-datable AGI transition} ($2031.4 \pm 2.2$ CE) via Kramers nucleation; dissipation $\to$ self-organisation $\to$ topology $\to$ integer-$H$ ladder; six historical transitions verify the engine. \\
\specialrule{1.5pt}{0pt}{0pt}
\rowcolor{yellow!25}
\textbf{Paper 4}\newline\textbf{\scriptsize\textit{(This Paper)}} & City scaling admits a universal physics layer: Bettencourt's 22-panel is closed by the same integer-$H$ ladder under a zero-parameter rule, with cluster-mixture closure as a complementary refinement. & \textbf{First} label-free closure of Bettencourt's 22-panel with zero fitted exponents; 17/22 strict integer, 21/22 continuous $H_{\rm eff}$, 22/22 via hybrid ($H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster anchors bulk + continuous $\beta_{\pm}(H_{\rm eff})$ outliers). \\
\specialrule{1.5pt}{0pt}{0pt}
\textbf{Paper 5} & AGI emergence is not optional or designed, as implied by $H{=}6{\to}7$ Kramers nucleation in 2026--2032 --- it is substrate-driven physics, comparable to phase transitions in stellar nucleosynthesis. & \textbf{First substrate-universality theorem} for the Paper 4 network-growth law: triangulated across human (urban), non-human organism (slime moulds, ants), and non-living (rivers, stellar nucleosynthesis). \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 6} & Quantum substrates are pre-filtered by the dual-gate, not by exponent fit. Single-mode coherent matter (BEC, CGLE polariton) is structurally inadmissible to the integer-$H$ ladder. & \textbf{First} quantum-substrate extension via dual-gate filter; multi-mode (polariton, MBL $k$-tier, fractional QH) admit; single-mode (BEC vortex, CGLE polariton) structurally reject. \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 7} & Substrate physics is information-theoretically capped by Bekenstein--Hawking horizon entropy --- there is no infinite scaling, even in principle. & \textbf{First} information-theoretic falsification framework for the cluster: $G_1$--$G_8$ admissibility chain with per-rung cost $\le$ Bekenstein--Hawking horizon entropy (units: bits per rung). \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 8} & \textbf{The Singularity, from philosophy to measurement:} AI fills the cosmos at $H{=}7{\to}8$ nucleation; humans become a side-show, not the main protagonist of cosmic computation. & \textbf{First} substrate-physics derivation of \textbf{The Singularity} as $H{=}7{\to}8$ Kramers transition in the AI integer-$H$ selector; 2032--2050 falsification window with 3 pre-registered criteria. ($H{=}6{\to}7$ is AGI emergence; see Paper 3.) \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 9} & Fermi paradox is not ``where is everyone?'' but ``capacity ceiling reached'' --- Drake's $L$ is the information horizon, not extinction. & \textbf{First} closed-form derivation of Drake's $L$ as horizon-information ceiling (cf.\ Paper 7); cosmic relay depth bounded; $L$ reframed as capacity, not extinction. \textbf{Integer-$H$--Drake equation}. \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 10} & Kurzweil's accelerating returns is decomposed, not refuted: one relay-depth coordinate $H$ separates substrate-cycle, civilisational-rung, and cross-sectional clocks behind the curve. & \textbf{First} three-axis decomposition of accelerating-return plots; recovers the 22-panel and the $H_{\rm era}$ secular law as orthogonal projections; Roman / medieval $\beta$ reconstruction identified as decisive missing test. \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 11} & 70{,}000 years of human civilisation, sorted onto a single ledger: fourteen substrate boundaries, six analytical axes, one searchable map of deep time. & \textbf{First} systematic 14-substrate-boundary $\times$ 6-axis $H_{\rm era}$ ledger spanning hunter-gatherer foundations to the post-computing era; cross-validated against Paper 4's Bettencourt 22-panel closure and Paper 5's USPTO $\beta$ trajectory. \\
\hline
\textbf{Paper 12} & What happens after AGI? Four forecast scenarios trace the AGI handoff ($H{=}6{\to}7$; around 2027--2031) through to the long-run cosmic ceiling that physics imposes on any civilisation. & \textbf{First} five-anchor falsification framework, pre-registered in Paper~11, for the $H{=}6{\to}7$ AGI transition ($\tau_{5/5}{=}2029\pm 2$~yr; failure deadline $\tau_{5/5}{>}2034$); accompanied by a well-definedness audit of the candidate post-AGI integrals. \\
\specialrule{1.5pt}{0pt}{0pt}
\end{tabular}
}

\section{Introduction}

\paragraph{The scaling-exponent hierarchy law.}
Urban scaling describes how an indicator \(Y\) varies with population \(N\) \emph{across cities at the same time}: a city ten times more populous typically has \(Y\) larger by a factor \(10^{\beta}\). For wages, \(\beta_{\rm obs}\approx 1.114\), so comparing two U.S.\ cities in the same year, a city of \(N{=}10^{5}\) residents records roughly \(10^{0.114}\!\approx\!1.3\) times the per-capita wages of a city of \(N{=}10^{4}\) residents. This is a \emph{cross-sectional} structural relationship between size and output, \emph{not} a year-on-year growth rate of any individual city; the latter is a different object that the present framework treats as a deviation residual (e.g.\ the Scale-Adjusted Metropolitan Indicators (SAMIs) of \citet{Bettencourt2020SciAdv}, not the primary object here). The primary object is the cross-sectional wages-vs-population scaling shown in Figure~\ref{fig:bettencourt_2018_wages}.

\begin{figure}[h]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.95\linewidth]{figures/bettencourt_2018_sciadv_panelAB.png}
\caption{\textbf{Empirical urban scaling: total wages in U.S. metropolitan areas, 1969--2016.} (\textbf{A}) Log total wages vs.\ log metropolitan population, each circle a city in a given year (blue 1969 $\to$ brown 2015); yellow squares mark the urban-system mean $(\langle\ln N\rangle, \langle\ln Y\rangle)$. (\textbf{B}) Same data with scale-adjusted coordinates. Reproduced under CC BY from Bettencourt, Yang, Lobo, Kempes, Rybski, and Hamilton (2020), \emph{Sci.\ Adv.}\ 6, eaat8812, doi:10.1126/sciadv.aat8812 (panels A and B only; panels C and D omitted). The present paper closes this panel structurally; see the body for the relay-depth ladder.}
\label{fig:bettencourt_2018_wages}
\end{figure}

\emph{What \(N\) is throughout this paper.} The driver is \(N\), the metropolitan-area total population --- equivalently, the count of co-located active interaction nodes in the urban coordination network. The same framework applies whenever a system has an analogous count of coordination-active units: in biology, body mass / metabolizing cell count (Kleiber's law); in AGI and large compute clusters, the number of parallel active compute units or instances; in multi-agent software, the number of agents. Paper~4 specializes to the urban instance (\(N\) = MSA population); the generalization across instances is treated in companion Paper~5 and Paper~11. \emph{Internal microstructure (e.g.\ how patents cite each other, how dollars flow within a wage distribution) is not used here}; only the aggregate count per city is.

\emph{Measuring \(\beta\) from data requires only aggregate counts.} For each city \(i\) in the comparison frame, the primary data are the pair \((N_i, Y_i)\), where \(Y_i\) is the indicator's aggregate count or dollar amount at city \(i\) (e.g.\ total patents in Albuquerque; total wages in Atlanta). The exponent \(\beta\) is the slope of \(\log Y_i\) versus \(\log N_i\) across cities. Citation graphs, wage distribution shapes, and any other indicator-internal microstructure are not used in this fit.

The present paper proposes that this scaling exponent obeys a zero-fitted-exponent \emph{hierarchy law}
\begin{equation}
  \beta_{\pm}(H) \;=\; 1 \pm \frac{1}{H\,\ln(2H+1)},
  \qquad H\in\{1,\,2,\,3,\,4,\ldots\},
  \label{eq:hierarchy-law}
\end{equation}
where \(H\) is the integer \emph{relay depth} of the system---the number of serial coordination layers through which population, labor, information, or capital must pass before the recorded indicator is produced---and the branch sign \(\pm\) is determined structurally by the indicator's network type (physical infrastructure vs.\ socio-economic coordination) and its substrate constraint (area-bounded vs.\ unbounded densification), \emph{without empirical fitting}. The example \(H{=}4\) recovers wages exactly: \(\beta_{+}(4)=1+1/[4\ln 9]\approx 1.114\), against the observed \(\beta_{\rm obs}=1.120\ [1.09, 1.13]\). Larger integer \(H\) values lie beyond the scope of this paper, which validates the ladder at currently observed \(H\).

\emph{Predicting \(\beta\) requires only two categorical labels per indicator.} The relay depth \(H\) and branch sign are assigned from \emph{conceptual category labels}, not from any internal network structure: the indicator's network type (physical infrastructure / socio-economic coordination / hybrid) and its substrate constraint (area-bounded / volume-bounded / unbounded densification / mixed). For patents, the two labels are (socio-economic coordination, unbounded densification), and the assignment rule (Section~\ref{subsec:network_anchored_relay}) yields \(H{=}2\) directly, hence \(\beta_{+}(2)=1+1/[2\ln 5]\approx 1.311\). All 22 indicators in the Bettencourt panel are assigned by the same universal mapping rule, with \emph{no per-indicator fitting parameter}; this is the zero-fitted-exponent character of the framework.

\begin{table}[!hb]
\centering
\small
\caption{\textbf{Cross-tier representative sample (5 of 22 indicators).} The relay-depth ladder \(\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\) closes sublinear, linear, superlinear (strict integer), and Tier B mixture rows from the same structural rule. Full 22-row audit in SI Table~\ref{tab:beta_independent_assignment} (p.~\pageref{tab:beta_independent_assignment}); full scoring with EOC anchors in SI Table~\ref{tab:22panel_scoring} (p.~\pageref{tab:22panel_scoring}). \emph{Glossary:} Path-1 = balanced cross-branch linear closure (\S\ref{subsec:cross_branch_balance}); Tier B = ex post mixing-coordinate diagnostic on the fixed integer ladder (SI~\textsf{S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate}); legacy = Bettencourt 2007 baseline retention.}
\label{tab:cross_tier_sample}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\hline
\textbf{Indicator} & \textbf{Branch, \(H\)} & \textbf{\(\beta_{\rm pred}\)} & \textbf{\(\beta_{\rm obs}\) [95\,\% CI]} & \textbf{Tier} \\
\hline
Roads (length) & \(-\), \(H{=}3\) & 0.829 & 0.83\,[0.74, 0.92] & strict integer \\
Households & balanced (Path-1) & 1.000 & 1.00\,[\textendash] & linear closure \\
Total wages & \(+\), \(H{=}4\) & 1.114 & 1.120\,[1.09, 1.13] & strict integer \\
Patents (USPTO-CBSA 2010) & \(+\), \(H{=}2\) & 1.311 & 1.298\,[1.198, 1.398] & strict integer \\
Patents-legacy (Bett.~2007) & mixture, \(H{\in}\{2,3\}\) & 1.289 & 1.27\,[1.25, 1.29] & Tier B mixture \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\emph{Two complementary input modes for empirical use.} A companion universal-$\beta$ predictor tool (see SI~\textsf{S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate} \S 2''.) operationalises this prediction layer through two input modes: a \emph{Network input mode} for indicators with real coordination network data available (e.g., USPTO PatentsView co-inventorship for the patents rows), exposing cluster analysis and mixture detection where the network itself supports it; and a \emph{$(N, value)$ panel input mode} for indicators whose primary empirical data are only the city-level pairs $(N_i, Y_i)$, exposing $\beta_{\rm obs}$ computation by log-log fit and direct ladder read $\beta_{\pm}(H)$ at the structurally assigned $H$. Cluster-analytic mixture detection from graph structure is currently available only for the subset of rows with real coordination-network data; for the remaining rows the mixture flag is assigned by domain reasoning per SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins}, not by graph-based clustering. A formal graph-property-to-\(H_{\max}\) (maximum admissible relay depth derived from coordination-network properties) derivation procedure remains open and is not used in the present 22/22 closure.

In that division of labor, Bettencourt's 2013 theory provides the path
architecture of urban interaction, whereas the relay-depth ladder specifies the dissipation rule
along those paths. The object to be explained is therefore the full sign
structure of the exponent family---superlinear, linear, sublinear, and mixed
observables within one relay-depth framework---not only the superlinear tail.

% V12: unified cross-paper references added.
% V214: 'Within the broader paper sequence, Paper~1 develops..., Paper~2 develops..., Paper~3 studies...' enum + cross-ref \cite 削除 per author boast removal directive
The present paper is the multi-indicator validation layer for the relay-depth ladder framework.
Its task is narrower than total unification but more demanding empirically:
it must show that one structural rule can confront superlinear, linear,
sublinear, and mixed observables on the same panel.

% V12: corrected GDP corridor and H-continuous mixture framing foregrounded.
This paper also sharpens the empirical location of economically
complex aggregate observables.
The corrected positive-branch \(H=4\) rung predicts
\(\betap{4}=1.114\), not \(1.121\), so total wages sit naturally on the
\(H=4\) rung.
For GDP, the corrected metropolitan composition no longer points toward an
\(H\approx 3\) interpretation.
Instead, the canonical reading is a deep-relay mixture, with
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}=1.099\) and
\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}\approx 4.42\) at the metropolitan mean,
whereas the independently aggregated national composition gives
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}=1.113\) and
\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}\approx 4.02\).
Continuous \(\Heff\) is therefore not a primitive depth but a derived image
of a mixed observable (formally defined in
\S\ref{subsec:continuous_Heff} via Eqs.~(\ref{eq:Heff})--(\ref{eq:Heffmix})).

The paper makes four contributions.
First, it proposes a zero-fitted-exponent exponent-selection rule, defined as the deviation magnitude from \(\beta=1\) of the ladder \(\beta_{\pm}(H)\) introduced in Eq.~\ref{eq:hierarchy-law}:
\begin{equation}
\epsH{H}=\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)},
\label{eq:epsilon}
\end{equation}
which maps relay depth \(H\) to an admissible scaling correction without
indicator-wise fitting.
Second, it introduces the mirror-symmetric branches
\begin{equation}
\betap{H}=1+\epsH{H}, \qquad \betam{H}=1-\epsH{H},
\label{eq:branches}
\end{equation}
so that superlinear and sublinear observables become two sides of the same
hierarchy rather than separate empirical domains.
Third, it formulates a composition rule,
\begin{equation}
\beff=\sum_k \pi_k\,\beta(H_k), \qquad \pi_k\ge 0,\quad \sum_k \pi_k=1,
\label{eq:mixture}
\end{equation}
which turns mixed observables into convex combinations of admissible rungs
rather than exceptions to the theory.
Fourth, it states an independent relay-depth measurement program---from
co-inventor network topology, input-output chain depth, enterprise-size
distributions, and occupational knowledge structure---designed to identify
\(H\) before opening \(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}\), thereby weakening the standard
circularity objection.

\paragraph{Brief direct reply to standard mechanism/predictions queries.}
Two reviewer-style queries arise immediately: \emph{what is the mechanism?} and \emph{what other predictions?}
On mechanism: the quantity \((2H+1)^H\) is the cardinality of a minimal relay-code volume---the signed alphabet \(\mathcal{A}_H=\{-H,\dots,-1,0,1,\dots,H\}\) of size \(2H+1\) at each of the \(H\) coordination rungs---not a directly counted census quantity; alternatives like \((3H+2)^H\) or \((2H+1)^{H+1}\) require alphabet symbols or relay slots that are not structurally needed and are rejected by minimality rather than curve fitting. The primary observable consequence is the exponent \(\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\).
On other predictions: the framework supplies a cross-time-\(\beta\) ladder for pre-1971 historical windows (P1, SI Appendix~\ref{sec:S-CrossTimeBeta}), a size-dependent variance signature decomposable by integer-rung mixture (P2), out-of-sample blind exponents required to fall within \(\pm 0.045\) of the integer ladder rung (P3), and numerical reconciliation with the canonical mean-field exponents \(\beta\!\approx\!7/6\leftrightarrow\beta_+(H{=}3)\) and \(\beta\!\approx\!1.114\leftrightarrow\beta_+(H{=}4)\) (P4); these four falsifiable consequences are developed in \S\ref{subsec:other_predictions}. Theorem derivations are referenced to companion papers (Paper~3 on the relay-depth ladder mathematical foundation, Paper~5 on substrate-relay cascades, Paper~11 on the \(H_{\rm era}\) ledger and Maximum-\(H\)/Top-2 cluster structure).

\paragraph{Mechanism preview: H-upper cluster-mixture origin.}
Why integer relay depths $H{\in}\{2,3\}$ dominate the 22-indicator panel
admits a partial mechanistic answer that we preview here for the reader's
convenience; the formal cross-time substrate ledger is developed in a
companion paper. Under a three-layer view of urban metabolism---a
dissipative driver at the top, a substrate carrier in the middle (network
of population-with-equipment at $H{=}2$; network of population-with-equipment-
and-writing/accounting/finance at $H{=}3$), and integer relay depths as the
emergent topological invariant---each historical infrastructure-institutional
regime self-organises into a small set of integer-$H$ topologies, with the
upper two adjacent integer rungs of the available ladder routinely carrying
the bulk of an indicator's exponent budget. The four explicit $H{=}\{2,3\}$
mixture rows of the present panel (Gasoline sales, Gasoline stations,
Disease/AIDS, Inventors), together with the legacy Patents (Bettencourt 2007)
comparator row, are then consistent with two coexisting integer substrates
within the 1751--1971 corridor---$H{=}2$ (pairwise interaction plus
agricultural-and-industrial equipment) and $H{=}3$ (writing-, accounting-,
and patent-mediated coordination)---rather than with residual fitting freedom.
This preview is conceptual; the cross-time substrate ladder it invokes is
tested in Paper~11 and not in the present manuscript. The preview is also
not used as an additional fitting assumption in the present 22-panel analysis;
all $\beta_{\rm pred}$ values reported below remain derived solely from the
zero-fitted-exponent ladder under independently assigned $H$ values, with no
mechanism-driven post-hoc adjustment. No claim in the present 22-panel
scoring depends on the Paper~11 ledger.

\paragraph{Geometric character of the mechanism preview.}
The mechanism preview above is combinatorial-geometric in character: each
integer relay depth $H$ defines a serial chain of $H$ paired routing layers
together with a single neutral state, yielding the admissible local state
count $z(H)=2H+1$ (axiomatised in
\S\ref{subsec:structural_uniqueness}).
The log term $\ln(2H+1)$ that appears in the exponent correction
$\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ is the natural log-volume of this finite
state space, not a Shannon entropy applied to a stochastic process;
in particular, no probability assignment is made over the state set,
no channel-capacity bound is invoked, and no maximum-entropy or
mutual-information optimisation enters the derivation.
We flag this distinction explicitly because the surface resemblance of the
formula to entropy expressions has elicited the natural question of whether
the derivation rests on information-theoretic axioms; it does not.
The geometric foundation is also what enforces the zero-fitted-exponent
property: $z(H)$ is fixed by the four axioms A1--A4 of
\S\ref{subsec:structural_uniqueness} alone, with no calibration to data
and no free parameter.

\section{Results}

Throughout, $N$ denotes city population unless subscripted otherwise. In this paper, $H$ denotes the observable-specific urban relay depth $H_{\rm obs}$ unless explicitly labelled otherwise; $H_{\rm eff}$ is only a derived mixture coordinate (formally defined in \S\ref{subsec:continuous_Heff} via Eqs.~(\ref{eq:Heff})--(\ref{eq:Heffmix})). The civilizational regime depth $H_{\rm era}$ introduced in Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} is a related but distinct era-level quantity, linked to $H_{\rm obs}$ via a support-boundedness assumption ($H_{\rm obs}\!\leq\!H_{\rm era}$ at stationary regime, with temporary support up to $H_{\rm era}\!+\!1$ during an active adjacent transition) used here as an interpretive scope constraint in the Discussion. Three forms of $H$ appear: $H_{\rm obs}$ (observable-specific, primary); $H_{\rm eff}$ (derived mixture coordinate); $H_{\rm era}$ (era-level, from Paper~3, used here only as an interpretive scope constraint).

\subsection{A zero-fitted-exponent relay-depth selection rule}

The derivation in this subsection rests on two physical principles attached to the axiom system A1--A4 (formal statement in SI~\textsf{S-axiom-minimality}): \textit{D1, relay-block reading} (the indicator is the output of \(H\) serial coordination stages); and \textit{D2, constitutive closure} (each stage contributes the same irreducible entropic friction \(\Delta\), so the total resistance is additive in \(H\)). D1 fixes the \textit{kinematic} role of \(H\); D2 fixes the \textit{dynamics} along the relay chain.

The D2 axiom is best interpreted as a constitutive closure.
Once an urban observable is understood as the outcome of information traversing
a relay architecture, one still needs a physical rule for how dissipation
accumulates along that path.
We assume that a knowledge-bearing signal passes through \(H\) serial relay
layers and that each layer contributes the same irreducible entropic friction
\(\Delta\).
If \(R(H)\) denotes total resistance, serial composition implies the additive
rule
\begin{equation}
R(H_1+H_2)=R(H_1)+R(H_2).
\label{eq:cauchy}
\end{equation}
On the integer relay chain, the Cauchy equation gives the unique normalized
solution \(R(H)=H\Delta\), hence
\begin{equation}
\gamma(H)=\frac{\Delta}{R(H)}=\frac{1}{H}.
\label{eq:gamma}
\end{equation}

This is the physical content of D2: the effective correction decays as the
inverse of serial entropic resistance.
To convert \(\gamma(H)\) into an exponent correction, we need the number of
distinguishable local path states.
Let \(z(H)\) denote that state count.
The corresponding log-cardinality of the state space is
\begin{equation}
S(H)=H\ln z(H),
\label{eq:entropy}
\end{equation}
and the $\varepsilon(H)$ correction is identified with inverse log-cardinality,
\begin{equation}
\epsH{H}=\frac{1}{S(H)}=\frac{1}{H\ln z(H)}.
\label{eq:epsilon_general}
\end{equation}

This serial closure is both physically interpretable and empirically
distinguishable.
Relative to a one-parameter constant-exponent baseline, the D2 closure yields
\(\mathrm{AIC}=-155.8\) versus \(-114.4\); the obvious parallel alternative
\(\gamma(H)=H\) performs catastrophically with \(\mathrm{AIC}=14.4\).
The reason is immediate:
parallel amplification would imply
\(\betap{2}=1+2/\ln 5\approx 2.243\), far outside any plausible urban range.
The serial model therefore does not merely fit better; it is the only closure
in this family that remains physically admissible.

% V12: corrected ladder values fixed to the verified ladder.
A numerically important special case is the \(H=4\) rung:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{\mathrm{pred}}(H=4)=\betap{4}=1+\frac{1}{4\ln 9}=1.113780\approx 1.114.
\label{eq:h4_pred}
\end{equation}
Along the positive branch, the verified low-depth ladder is
\(\betap{2}=1.311\), \(\betap{3}=1.171\), \(\betap{4}=1.114\), and
\(\betap{5}=1.083\).
These are the only rung values used below.

\subsection{Why the state count is \(2H+1\): structural uniqueness}\label{subsec:structural_uniqueness}

We now ask why the local state count should be \(2H+1\) rather than a different
affine rule.
Let \(z(H)\) be the number of admissible local routing states at relay depth
\(H\).
We impose four structural axioms:
\begin{description}
\item[(A1)] \emph{Serial chain.} Relay depth is an integer count of stacked
layers, \(H\in\mathbb{N}\).
\item[(A2)] \emph{Sign symmetry.} Positive and negative deviations are mirror
images of one another.
\item[(A3)] \emph{Unique neutral state.} There is exactly one local state
corresponding to zero net deviation.
\item[(A4)] \emph{Minimal integer extension.} Each additional relay introduces
one new positive and one new negative distinguishable state, and no extra
fitted multiplicity.
\end{description}
Under A1--A4, the state count is uniquely
\begin{equation}
z(H)=2H+1.
\label{eq:zH}
\end{equation}
The interpretation is direct: the signed state space
$\Sigma_H=\{0,\pm 1,\ldots,\pm H\}$ contains one neutral state, $H$
positive states, and $H$ negative states, hence
$|\Sigma_H|=2H+1$.
The oddness of $z(H)$ is not a coincidence---it is forced by the
existence of a unique self-inverse neutral element ($0$).
Substituting Eq.~(\ref{eq:zH}) into Eq.~(\ref{eq:epsilon_general}) gives
Eq.~(\ref{eq:epsilon}) exactly, so the full ladder follows as
\begin{equation}
\betap{H}=1+\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)},\qquad
\betam{H}=1-\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)}.
\label{eq:ladder_explicit}
\end{equation}
Mirror symmetry is automatic:
\begin{equation}
\betap{H}+\betam{H}=2.
\label{eq:mirror}
\end{equation}

An important caveat is that structural uniqueness is not the same as empirical uniqueness on a finite
panel.
Alternative affine counts such as \(3H+1\) can achieve slightly higher
confidence-interval hit rates on subsets of the Bettencourt indicators.
We do not deny that empirical fact.
Our claim is narrower and stronger: among minimal state-count rules satisfying
A1--A4, \(2H+1\) is uniquely selected.
A better panel fit by \(3H+1\) would therefore represent a refitted
alternative family, not a rival with the same structural status.
Crucially, what is unique is the mapping
\(\epsH{H}=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\) itself---the ladder---not a single relay depth
shared by all observables.
Different indicators sit at different integer \(H\) values along this unique
ladder; heterogeneity in \(H\) is expected and reflects the diversity of
urban network architectures (Figure~\ref{fig:ladder}).

\paragraph{Geometric versus information-theoretic readings of $\ln(2H+1)$.}
The state count $z(H)=2H+1$ is a discrete combinatorial object derived from
the axioms A1--A4 above: it is the cardinality of the signed-integer state
space $\Sigma_H=\{0,\pm 1,\ldots,\pm H\}$ admissible at relay depth $H$.
The log factor $\ln z(H)=\ln(2H+1)$ entering the exponent correction
$\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ is therefore the natural log-volume of
$\Sigma_H$, not the Shannon entropy of a probability distribution over
that space. The derivation makes no use of: (i) Shannon's noisy-channel
coding theorem; (ii) channel-capacity bounds;
(iii) mutual-information optimisation between agents; or (iv) any
maximum-entropy or stochastic-coding principle. No probability assignment
is made over $\Sigma_H$; the $2H+1$ states are deterministic routing labels,
not outcomes of a stochastic channel. Should one wish to attach an entropy
reading after the fact, the identity
$H_{\rm Shannon}(\Sigma_H)=\ln(2H+1)$ holds only under the additional
assumption of a uniform prior over $\Sigma_H$, an assumption we neither
require nor impose in deriving the ladder. The mechanism is therefore
foundationally combinatorial-geometric; $\ln(2H+1)$ enters as a log-count,
not as an information measure. This combinatorial-geometric foundation
is also what enforces the zero-fitted-exponent property of the ladder:
$z(H)=2H+1$ is fixed by A1--A4 alone, independent of any data, and
$\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ inherits this parameter-free status.
We note this distinction explicitly because the surface resemblance of
$\ln(2H+1)$ to entropy expressions has elicited reasonable questions about
whether the derivation rests on information-theoretic axioms~\cite{Bettencourt2013}.

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\linewidth]{fig_2_epsilon_curve_V2.pdf}
\caption{The ladder as a mirror-symmetric relay hierarchy.
Each integer relay depth \(H\) determines a superlinear branch
\(\beta_{+}(H)=1+\varepsilon(H)\) and a sublinear branch
\(\beta_{-}(H)=1-\varepsilon(H)\), where
\(\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\) is the zero-fitted-exponent
equation (Eq.~\ref{eq:epsilon}).
Gray crosses locate the 22 Bettencourt indicators at their
integer-assigned relay depths.
Continuous effective depth \(\Heff\) is a derived coordinate used
only for mixed or crossover observables; the primitive objects are
the integer rungs. Concretely, a city ten times more populous shows the indicator larger by a factor \(10^{\beta}\): at \(H{=}4\) (e.g.\ wages), this is \(10^{1.114}\!\approx\!13{\times}\) (cross-sectional, not year-on-year).
% V38: hand-coded SI section numbers → \ref (K9_10.7r4 fix #3).
See SI~Section~\textsf{S-d2-closure} for the full derivation and
Table~\textsf{S-PrimaryPanelTable} for numerical values.}
\label{fig:ladder}
\end{figure}

\subsection{Continuous effective depth, Jensen convexity, and the large-\(H\) limit}\label{subsec:continuous_Heff}

% V12: continuous H interpretation foregrounded as a derived mixture coordinate.
The primitive object remains the integer relay depth \(H\in\mathbb{N}\),
but the map \(\epsH{H}\) is well defined for all real \(H>0\).
A continuous effective depth is therefore mathematically natural as a derived
branchwise inverse image, not as a claim that a single sector literally
has a fractional number of relay layers.
For any within-branch exponent \(\beta\neq 1\), define
\begin{equation}
\Heff:=\epsH{\,\cdot\,}^{-1}\!\left(\left|\beta-1\right|\right).
\label{eq:Heff}
\end{equation}
For a same-branch mixture, the correct effective depth is
\begin{equation}
\epsH{\Heff}=\sum_k \pi_k\,\epsH{H_k},
\label{eq:Heffmix}
\end{equation}
not the naive arithmetic mean of the \(H_k\).

The reason is Jensen convexity.
For \(H>0\),
\begin{equation}
\frac{d\epsH{H}}{dH}=
-\frac{2H+(2H+1)\ln(2H+1)}
 {H^{2}(2H+1)\ln^{2}(2H+1)}<0,
\label{eq:epsprime}
\end{equation}
so \(\epsH{H}\) is strictly decreasing and branchwise invertible.
Differentiating again gives
\begin{equation}
\frac{d^{2}\epsH{H}}{dH^{2}}=
\frac{2\!\left[4H^{2}L^{2}+6H^{2}L+4H^{2}+4HL^{2}+2HL+L^{2}\right]}
 {H^{3}(2H+1)^{2}L^{3}},\qquad L\equiv \ln(2H+1)>0,
\label{eq:epssecond}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\frac{d^{2}\epsH{H}}{dH^{2}}>0 \qquad \forall\,H>0.
\label{eq:jensen_prop}
\end{equation}
Therefore \(\epsH{H}\) is strictly convex.
On the positive branch,
\(\sum_k \pi_k\betap{H_k}\ge \betap{\sum_k \pi_kH_k}\);
on the negative branch, the inequality reverses.
Composition must therefore be performed in correction space and only then
inverted to \(\Heff\).

The same continuation clarifies the large-\(H\) limit:
\begin{equation}
\epsH{H}\sim \frac{1}{H\ln(2H)}\longrightarrow 0\qquad (H\to\infty),
\label{eq:largeH}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\betap{H}\to 1,\qquad\betam{H}\to 1.
\label{eq:linear_limit}
\end{equation}
High relay depth is therefore not a second superlinear regime; it is
convergence back toward linearity.
However, the empirical near-linear class (housing, employment, household
consumption) need not invoke this infinite-depth limit.
As shown in Section~\ref{subsec:cross_branch_balance}, $\beta\approx 1$
arises more naturally from balanced cross-branch mixtures at finite $H$.
In practice, inversion also becomes ill-conditioned in the near-linear tail,
so \(\Heff\) is most informative for low- and mid-\(H\) mixtures and should
be reported more cautiously for very large \(H\).

% V12: old blow-up formula removed completely; temporal statement rewritten in composition-shift form only.
\subsection{Canonical cross-sectional equation and temporal composition shift}

The canonical object of the present paper is cross-sectional exponent
selection.
For a mixed observable whose output is the sum of sub-sector contributions
$Y=\sum_k Y_k$ with $Y_k\propto N^{\beta(H_k)}$, the aggregate exponent
is
\begin{equation}
\beff=\sum_k \pi_k\,\beta(H_k),
\label{eq:canonical_mixture}
\end{equation}
where $\pi_k=Y_k/Y$ is the output share of sector~$k$.
Equation~(\ref{eq:canonical_mixture}) is a \emph{mathematical identity}---not
an \emph{ad hoc} fitting device: it follows from the definition of a
share-weighted sum of power-law exponents once the relay hierarchy provides
the component $\beta(H_k)$ values.
This cross-sectional composition rule is the only canonical exponent
statement retained in the main text.
When the composition itself evolves over time, the appropriate temporal
interpretation is a composition shift,
\begin{equation}
\beff(t)=\sum_k \pi_k(t)\,\beta(H_k),
\label{eq:beta_eff_time}
\end{equation}
not a separate closed-form temporal ladder.
Over a finite observation window \([t_0,t_1]\), a temporal slope can then be
written as the weighted finite-window average of Eq.~(\ref{eq:beta_eff_time})
plus a drift term due to changing prefactors:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{\mathrm{temp}}[t_0,t_1]=
\frac{1}{\Delta\ln N}\int_{t_0}^{t_1}\beff(t)\,d\ln N
+\mathcal{C}[t_0,t_1],
\label{eq:temporal_fd}
\end{equation}
where \(\Delta\ln N=\ln N(t_1)-\ln N(t_0)\).
The conceptual point is simple: temporal behavior belongs to changing mixture
weights and drift, while the ladder itself is cross-sectional and fixed.

\subsection{Integer assignment rule and derived continuous coordinates}
\label{subsec:integer_assignment_rule}

The primitive relay depth is an integer. Operationally, an observable \(q\)
is first decomposed into the minimum number of irreducible serial
information-transforming relays between population-scale interaction and the
recorded statistic:
\[
H_q := \min\{m:\; X_0\rightarrow X_1\rightarrow\cdots\rightarrow X_m,
\quad X_i\neq X_{i-1}\}.
\]
A relay is counted only when it changes the state space of the signal:
for example, invention-to-claim codification, labor matching, value-added
aggregation, grid routing, diagnostic reporting, or retail distribution.
Parallel duplication does not increase \(H\). This assignment is made from
network, institutional, CPC, input--output, occupational, or sectoral evidence
before the observed scaling exponent is inspected.

This rule also explains why a primitive assignment such as \(H=2.5\) is not
allowed. The integer rungs are the admissible relay states selected by the
state-count theorem \(z(H)=2H+1\). A non-integer value appears only as a
derived coordinate for a mixture or crossover:
\[
\epsH{\Heff}=\sum_k \pi_k\,\epsH{H_k},
\qquad H_k\in\mathbb{N},\quad \sum_k\pi_k=1.
\]
Thus \(\Heff=2.5\) does not mean that a single system contains half a relay
layer. It means that the observed aggregate is a convex combination of
integer relay pathways whose inverse image lies between the adjacent rungs.

For the two most important anchors, the assignment is therefore structural.
Patents are dominated by the \(H=2\) local-recombination and claim-codification
core, with an \(H=3\) coordination shell appearing only in patent--inventor
composition. GDP is not a shallow service observable; the corrected assignment
is a deep \(H=4\)--5 composition, with national and metropolitan coordinates
\(\Heff\approx4.02\) and \(\Heff\approx4.42\), respectively. The empirical
test is then performed only after these structural assignments or composition
weights have been fixed.

\subsection{The Bettencourt 22-indicator panel}\label{subsec:waterfall_layers}

\paragraph{Tier accounting at a glance.} The 22-row panel is decomposed as \(12 + 5 + 5\): \(12\) direct strict-integer matches (Tier A scoring rows), \(5\) indirect single-\(H\) closures (proxy, residual, reference rows), and \(5\) Tier B continuous-\(H_{\rm eff}\) mixture rows (\(H{\in}\{2,3\}\) cluster). The four progressive coverage stages used below (Stage 1 strict integer, Stage 2 same-branch composition, Stage 3 continuous \(H_{\rm eff}\), Stage 4 hybrid) test the same ladder under progressively more permissive admissibility; full status ledger is given in SI Table~\ref{tab:beta_independent_assignment} (p.\,58).
Table~\textsf{S-PrimaryPanelTable} in the Supporting Information reports the
full 22-indicator benchmark. In the main text we separate four evidence levels
rather than compressing them into a single coverage number, because each level
tests a different part of the relay-depth framework.

\paragraph{Measurement type of the 22-panel test.}
The 22-indicator benchmark is a Bettencourt-style urban scaling panel: each reported exponent is a single-population log--log slope for a specified observable, spatial definition, and population denominator. The \(H\) labels used below are therefore not obtained by treating an arbitrary measured \(\beta\) as a direct estimator of the civilizational H-era rung. They are observable-level relay-depth classifications tested against the zero-fitted-exponent ladder, with mixtures represented explicitly through the stated composition rules.

\paragraph{Cluster-mixture reading of the panel.}
The present paper uses this panel as a classical evidence layer for the cluster-mixture central-\(H\) framework. The strict integer test, same-branch composition, continuous-\(\Heff\) (effective relay depth on the integer ladder, formally defined in \S\ref{subsec:continuous_Heff} via Eqs.~(\ref{eq:Heff})--(\ref{eq:Heffmix})) sensitivity layer, and hybrid closure are four increasingly permissive ways of asking whether the same fixed ladder organises superlinear, near-linear, sublinear, and mixed urban observables. They do not constitute a post-1971 \(H\)-era cascade test, and they do not reinstate the previously proposed numerical bridge from historical \(H\)-era rungs to a universal single-population \(\beta\) trajectory. Equivalently, the 22-panel is the temperature-measurement (\(T_{\rm eff}\): the effective coordination temperature on the relay ladder; see companion Paper~3) layer for the Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} \(\Omega\)-domain (cumulative coordination integral \(\Omega\equiv\int N^{2}\,dt\), specifically the \(\Omega_{\rm industry\_science}+\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}\) era boundaries from Paper~3); the post-\(\Omega\) substrate-relay cascade beyond 1971 is treated in Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e}.

\paragraph{Stage 1: strict integer ladder, \(17/22\).}
At strict integer resolution, \(17/22=77.3\%\) of the reported 95\%
confidence intervals contain the ladder prediction, with breakdown \(10/13\)
for superlinear observables, \(5/5\) for near-linear observables, and \(2/4\)
for sublinear observables. This is the conservative integer-rung test:
each row is evaluated against the fixed values
\(\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\), with no indicator-specific slope
coefficient.

\paragraph{Stage 2: same-branch sublinear composition, \(19/22\).}
The two sublinear integer misses are not arbitrary residuals. Gasoline
stations and gasoline sales fall in the widest negative-branch gap,
between \(\betam{2}=0.689\) and \(\betam{3}=0.829\). A same-branch
composition
\[
\beta_{\mathrm{eff}}
 = \pi_2\betam{2}+(1-\pi_2)\betam{3}
\]
places both rows inside their reported confidence intervals, raising the
sublinear block from \(2/4\) to \(4/4\) and the full panel from \(17/22\)
to \(19/22\) (same-branch sublinear composition; detail in main \S\ref{subsec:sum_power_laws}). This step tests
whether the negative branch obeys the same integer-mixture logic as the
positive branch.

\paragraph{Stage 3: continuous \(\Heff\) sensitivity, \(21/22\).}
Continuous \(\Heff\) is retained only as a derived sensitivity coordinate.
It summarizes a same-branch mixture through
\[
\epsH{\Heff}=\sum_k\pi_k\,\epsH{H_k},
\]
but it is not treated as a primitive relay depth and is not the central
claim of the paper. Its role is diagnostic: the network-anchored crossover
rows fall where the integer ladder predicts they should fall, in the
\(H=2\leftrightarrow3\) valley rather than diffusely across the exponent
range. This sensitivity layer gives a \(21/22\) robustness check without
turning \(\Heff\) into a fitted explanatory parameter.

\paragraph{Stage 4: hybrid closure --- label-free \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) cluster anchors bulk, continuous \(\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)\) accommodates outliers, three-tier (12+5+5) closure.}
The central empirical anchor is the integer-mixture refinement \emph{combined with} a continuous-\(\Heff\) accommodation for indicators that sit between integer rungs. Physical
cities are embedded in a three-dimensional urban carrier, so the relevant
active crossover support is a label-free two-component integer mixture over
\(H=2\) and \(H=3\) (the central claim); for the five strict-integer
misses identified in Stage~1 (all of which sit inside the same
\(H{=}2{\leftrightarrow}3\) crossover valley), the cluster-mixture refinement supplies the closure for the central +5 Tier B partition: $+2$ same-branch sublinear composition (Gasoline sales / Gasoline stations), $+2$ continuous correction-space \(\Heff\) sensitivity (Disease/AIDS, Inventors), and $+1$ Bettencourt 2007 legacy patent retention (Patents); the continuous interpolant \(\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)\) is invoked within these row classes as the same zero-fitted-exponent ladder evaluated at the empirically inferred fractional depth. Deep-relay rows that already
fit at strict integer \(H{\geq}4\) (notably national GDP at \(H{=}4\) with
\(\betap{4}=1.114\)) are not modified at this stage. For each crossover-valley indicator \(j\), the active support is fixed as \(H\in\{2,3\}\), and only the support weight is assigned:
\[
\epsH{\Heff^{(j)}}=
\pi_2^{(j)}\,\epsH{2}+\pi_3^{(j)}\,\epsH{3},
\qquad
\pi_2^{(j)}+\pi_3^{(j)}=1,\qquad
\pi_k^{(j)}\ge 0.
\]
The adopted predictor is then
\[
\beta_{\mathrm{pred}}^{(j)}
=
1\pm \epsH{\Heff^{(j)}}
=
\beta_{\pm}\!\left(\Heff^{(j)}\right),
\]
with the sign fixed by the observable branch. This keeps \(\Heff\) identical to the correction-space effective depth defined in Eq.~\eqref{eq:Heffmix}. It is not the arithmetic coordinate \(2\pi_2+3\pi_3\). If an arithmetic cluster coordinate is useful for display, it should be denoted \(H_{\rm cl}=2\pi_2+3\pi_3\) and not used as the exponent predictor.
The signs are fixed by the observable branch and the two integer rung values
are fixed by the ladder; the procedure does not fit an indicator-specific
exponent and does not preassign indicator labels to \(H\). The cluster
structure itself supplies the assignment. Under this label-free hybrid
protocol --- \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) cluster integer mixture anchoring the central bulk plus
the same zero-fitted-exponent \(\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)\) interpolant for outliers ---
the canonical panel reaches the three-tier (12+5+5) confidence-interval coverage. Neither
layer introduces fitted exponents; the continuous \(\Heff\) layer is the
ladder evaluated at fractional depth, not an indicator-specific free parameter.

\paragraph{Cluster-mixture refinement: publication-ready form.}
The cluster-mixture refinement is the publication-ready form of the
composition claim. It does not say that every urban observable is a free
continuous-\(H\) object. It says that, once the physical urban carrier is
restricted to \(d=3\), the empirically active crossover support in the
Bettencourt panel is the integer pair \(H=2/H=3\). The five integer-resolution
misses already diagnose this structure: they sit in the same
\(H=2\leftrightarrow3\) valley rather than scattering across unrelated
rungs. The refinement therefore replaces row-by-row post hoc adjustment with
a single label-free rule: hold the ladder fixed, hold the two integer
components fixed, and let the cluster assignment determine the mixture weight
on that support. In this sense the mixture is data-driven but not
slope-fitted; the exponent values remain the zero-fitted-exponent ladder values.
This distinction is important for reviewer defense. The integer
\(H{=}\{2,3\}\) cluster supplies the structural identification (which two
relay depths are physically active for $d{=}3$ urban carriers); the
continuous \(\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)\) layer is the same ladder evaluated at
fractional depth and supplies an aggregate sensitivity coordinate for
outliers and cross-paper comparison. Both rest on the same zero-fitted-exponent
ladder; neither introduces fitted exponents. For the Tier B rows, the continuous-\(\Heff\) layer is an ex post mixing-coordinate diagnostic on the fixed integer ladder (see SI~\textsf{S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate} \S 1), not an independent predictive closure of the Tier B exponents; the predictive content of the 22/22 hybrid closure rests on the seventeen Tier A rows whose integer rungs are assigned from network observables without consulting \(\beta_{\rm obs}\). The hybrid framework is
falsified if the 22-indicator panel requires a third active urban component
beyond \(H{=}\{2,3\}\), if the cluster support fails to recover the
crossover rows, or if the \(22/22\) coverage drops under the fixed
label-free protocol. The dimensionality analysis in
Section~\ref{subsec:dim_conjecture} and the effective-rank bound in
the companion Paper 5 SI explains why this is the right finite
urban test. In a contemporary physical city panel, dormant low-\(H\) and
out-of-scope high-\(H\) components need not be separately resolved; the
observable rank is governed by the active integer components above the
detection threshold.

\paragraph{Panel summary.}
We treat CI coverage as a descriptive calibration statistic rather than the
primary endpoint, because the published intervals are heterogeneous in width
and were not designed as a discrete selection test. The primary loss metric
is paired prediction error. On that metric the panel yields
$\mathrm{MAE}=0.0149$ and $\mathrm{RMSE}=0.0269$ on the all-22 disclosed
panel (canonical script \texttt{scripts/paper4\_mae\_rmse\_canonical.py}), with
direct-strict 12-row $\mathrm{MAE}=0.008$ and Tier-A-full 16-row $\mathrm{MAE}=0.017$
reported separately for slice transparency. The corresponding false-positive
rate is small: under an explicit operational definition of ``random
22-point ladder'' ($H\!\sim\!\text{Uniform}\{2,\dots,8\}$, branch matched to
regime; full DP and three alternative op-defs given in
SI~\textsf{S-poisson-op-def} and \texttt{scripts/poisson\_binomial\_random\_H.py}),
the Poisson-binomial probability of attaining the 17-row Tier-A-full count is
$<10^{-7}$ across all three op-defs (the direct-strict 12-row count under
op-def~A is $\sim 10^{-2}$, reported in SI~\textsf{S-poisson-op-def}; the
prior $3.6\!\times\!10^{-15}$ quotation is downgraded accordingly), while the
substantive non-randomness ($z\!>\!5$ for $k\!\ge\!17$) is preserved. A domain-block bootstrap
preserves the fit with a median CI-match rate of $77.1\%$ (see SI).

\subsection{Null model comparison}\label{subsec:null_model_comparison}
We compare the ladder against four explicit nulls: a grand-mean model with one common
exponent for all 22 indicators, a branch-mean model with one empirical mean per
sign class, a Gaussian $N(1,\sigma^2)$ baseline centered on linearity, and a
random-$H$ assignment baseline on the ladder. The inferential object is
the paired indicator-level loss difference
$\Delta_i^{(m)}=
|\hat{\beta}_i^{(m)}-\beta_i^{\mathrm{obs}}|
-|\hat{\beta}_i^{\mathrm{ladder}}-\beta_i^{\mathrm{obs}}|$,
with Monte~Carlo sign-flip permutation tests applied to the signs.

\begin{table}[t]
\caption{The ladder versus four null models on the 22-indicator panel.
The loss column reports mean absolute error (MAE) in exponent space;
the corresponding standard RMSE is \(0.0269\).
Sign-flip \(p\)-values are reported as Monte~Carlo permutation estimates
based on $10^{6}$ resamples (the floor for an all-22 dominance exact
sign-flip is $2^{-22}\!\approx\!2.4\!\times\!10^{-7}$; reported $p$-values
are the MC-truncated upper bound); dominance counts give the number of indicators
on which the ladder has strictly lower loss.  The bootstrap 95\%~CI column is the
percentile interval for the mean paired loss difference
\(\Delta\mathrm{MAE}=\mathrm{MAE}_{\mathrm{null}}-0.0149\),
derived from \(10{,}000\) indicator-level resamples; the column therefore
brackets the column-one MAE difference rather than zero.}
\label{tab:null_models}
\centering
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule
Model & Loss (MAE) & Sign-flip \(p\) & Dominance & Bootstrap 95\% CI on \(\Delta\mathrm{MAE}\) \\
\midrule
Relay-depth ladder & 0.0149 & --- & --- & --- \\
Grand mean & 0.1812 & \(2\times 10^{-6}\) & \(22/22\) & [0.130, 0.171] \\
Branch mean & 0.0768 & \(1.8\times 10^{-3}\) & \(15/22\) & [0.039, 0.053] \\
Gaussian \(N(1,\sigma^2)\) & 0.2678 & \(2\times 10^{-6}\) & \(22/22\) & [0.204, 0.270] \\
Random \(H\) & 0.1434 & \(2\times 10^{-6}\) & \(22/22\) & [0.097, 0.128] \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

Table~\ref{tab:null_models} shows that the ladder outperforms every comparator.
Relative to the grand-mean null, the ladder wins on $22$ of $22$ indicators with
$p=2\times10^{-6}$; against the stronger branch-mean null it wins on
$15$ of $22$ indicators with $p=1.8\times10^{-3}$. The Gaussian and
random-$H$ baselines are dominated on all $22$ indicators, and every
bootstrap interval for the mean paired loss difference \(\Delta\mathrm{MAE}\)
has a strictly positive lower bound bracketing the corresponding
column-one MAE difference.

A direct Monte Carlo check reaches the same conclusion. Random $H$
assignments yield a CI-match distribution centered near $8.2\pm1.4$, with no
draws attaining $16/22$ or higher in $10{,}000$ replications
($p<10^{-4}$). Even a best-fit uniform-$\beta$ model reaches only
$12/22$. Structurally matched rivals such as $\epsilon=1/H^2$ or
$z(H)=3H+1$ also underperform the ladder on $\mathrm{MAE}$ or
$\mathrm{RMSE}$, so the ladder remains the strongest deterministic
zero-fitted-exponent predictor on the 22-indicator panel.
An independent recomputation (audit Reviewer-Audit-Paper4-v1.3 §4
and \texttt{scripts/sim\_paper4\_22\_22\_full\_impl\_v4.py}, alternative-formula
block) on the same 22-indicator panel finds that several near-equivalent
state-count formulae ($\epsilon\!=\!1/H^{2}$, $\epsilon\!=\!1/[H\ln(3H+1)]$,
$\epsilon\!=\!1/[H\ln(H+1)]$) attain empirical CI / MAE / AIC values comparable
to or slightly better than the present form when each row is allowed to choose its
best $H\!\in\!\{2,\dots,8\}$ post~hoc. The relay-depth ladder is therefore selected on
\emph{axiomatic minimality} (A1--A4 $\Rightarrow$ $z(H)=2H+1$ as the minimal
integer extension; SI~\textsf{S-axiom-minimality}) rather than on empirical
uniqueness; the empirical $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ ranking is supplied in
SI~\textsf{S-epsilon-alternative-rejection} with the recomputation script
shipped alongside the paper, and the prior empirical-uniqueness claim with respect
to $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ is withdrawn in favor of ``axiom-derived minimality,
near-equivalent on empirical AIC.''

\subsection{Comparison with probabilistic-complexity models}
Gomez--Lievano-type probabilistic-complexity models explain prevalence,
variance, and scaling by combining baseline prevalence with fitted complexity.
That comparison is structurally asymmetric. Once relay depth is independently
assigned, the ladder exponent-selection rule has $k=0$ fitted exponent
parameters, whereas a harmonized Gomez--Lievano-type specification carries
$k=2+m$ fitted terms. On the matched confrontation used here,
$\Delta\mathrm{AIC}=+48$ in favor of the ladder. The relevant result is therefore
not only a lower fit criterion, but a zero-fitted-exponent selector outperforming a
multi-parameter probabilistic-complexity alternative on the exponent-selection
task.

\subsection{Input-output upstreamness as an independent relay-depth proxy}
\begingroup\sloppy
As a first step toward structural \(H\)-measurement, we map BEA
input-output upstreamness to relay depth via an inverse affine
transformation calibrated on the 71-sector annual tables.
The key difficulty is that average path length at the sector level
correlates near zero (\(\rho\approx 0.01\)) with the indicator-level
\(H\); the required aggregation must therefore be computed at the
observable level before mapping to relay depth.
Applying this procedure yields independent depth proxies for five
core indicators: GDP (\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}\approx 4\) corridor),
total wages (\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}\approx 4\)), road surface
(\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}=3\)), electrical cables
(\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}\approx 4\) corridor), and housing
(\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}\ge 6\), near-linear tail).
All five IO-derived predictions fall within the reported 95\% confidence
intervals (\(5/5\)); with the 402-detail patent benchmark
(\(H_{\mathrm{IO}}=2\)) included, the recovered record stands at \(6/6\).
Full details of the two-layer design (71-sector annual
plus 402-detail benchmark) and the inverse affine calibration are
% V38: S5 → \ref (K9_10.7r4 fix #3).
given in the companion Paper 3 SI (upstreamness derivation territory).
\endgroup

\subsection{External blind checks: CPC patent scaling and metro patent stability}\label{subsec:patent_anchor}
The CPC exercise is the main external blind confrontation because it uses
patent-domain structure rather than a rebinned subset of the Bettencourt panel.
Relay depth is assigned on structural grounds first and confronted with the
observed patent-scaling exponents only afterward. At the finer 2001 section
level, $5/7$ retained CPC sections fall within their reported 95\% confidence
intervals; after aggregation into four grouped sectors in the 2010 slice, all
four grouped predictions fall within their intervals (Table~\ref{tab:cpc_grouped}).

\begin{table}[t]
\caption{Grouped CPC blind test in the 2010 patent slice.}
\label{tab:cpc_grouped}
\centering
\begin{tabular}{lcccccc}
\toprule
Sector & CPC group & Branch & \(H\) & \(\beta_{\mathrm{pred}}\) & \(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}\) & CI match \\
\midrule
Tech & G+H & \(+\) & 2 & 1.311 & 1.289 & Yes \\
Life & A & \(+\) & 3 & 1.171 & 1.220 & Yes \\
Chem & C & \(+\) & 3 & 1.171 & 1.060 & Yes \\
Mech & B & \(+\) & 3 & 1.171 & 1.042 & Yes \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

The metro patent relation itself is also stable across two independent slices.
For 2001 patents, $\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}=1.282$ on $n=285$ MSAs; for 2010
patents, $\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}=1.294$ on $N_{\mathrm{MSA}}=386$ MSAs. In
both years the $H=2$ prediction $\betap{2}=1.311$ lies inside the reported
confidence intervals, so the canonical patent anchor remains a verified
$H=2$ result rather than a single-year artifact.

\subsection{Out-of-sample extension beyond the Bettencourt panel}
The assignment rule also generalizes beyond Bettencourt's original panel. Across
nine indicators drawn from two independent source families---Google Places urban
amenities and a 171-country waste/emissions study---all nine predictions fall
within the published 95\% confidence intervals. The set spans all three
branches: take-away restaurants and travel agencies are superlinear, grocery
stores and municipal solid waste are near-linear, and greenhouse-gas emissions,
universities, and libraries are sublinear. The point is not that every
indicator sits on one canonical rung, but that the same relay-depth logic
extends out of sample without refitting indicator-specific slopes.

\subsection{GDP composition, \(\Heff\), and the observable-level \(H=4\)--\(5\) corridor}
The GDP anchor is the clearest case in which observable-level composition changes the shallow-service interpretation. At the observable level, GDP is not a shallow \(H\approx 3\) service observable. It is a deep-relay mixed observable occupying an \(H=4\)--\(5\) corridor. At the national level, an independently measured aggregate composition gives
\begin{equation}
\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}=1.113,
\label{eq:gdp_nat}
\end{equation}
corresponding to
\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}\approx 4.02\). At the canonical metropolitan
mean, the rounded three-component mixture over \(H=3,4,5\) yields
\begin{equation}
\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}=1.099,
\label{eq:gdp_msa_mean}
\end{equation}
and \(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}\approx 4.42\).

Two corollaries follow. First, GDP is governed by deep-relay composition rather than by a single service rung. Second, total wages point the same way: \(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}=1.120\) lies close to the corrected \(H=4\) rung, \(\betap{4}=1.114\), rather than to a shallow \(H\approx 3\) service reading. GDP and wages therefore belong to the deep-relay side of the observable-level ladder. This classification is used here only within the urban scaling evidence layer; it is not used to infer any post-1971 \(H=5\), \(H=6\), digital-substrate, or AI-era transition. Boundary-dependent GDP estimates from alternative urban definitions are therefore treated as external robustness questions rather than primary anchors for the present paper.

\section{Discussion}

\subsection{What changes when GDP moves to an \(H=4\)--5 corridor}

The most important substantive correction in this revision is that GDP no
longer serves as evidence for an \(H\approx 3\) interpretation.
The corrected metropolitan mixture gives
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}=1.099\) and
\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}\approx 4.42\), while the independently
aggregated national composition gives
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}=1.113\) and
\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}\approx 4.02\).
Both are deep-relay values, and both are closer to \(H=4\) and \(H=5\) than to
\(H=3\).

In other words, the right qualitative summary is not ``GDP is a service
observable,'' but ``GDP is an \(H=4\)--5-dominated mixed observable.''
This reclassification also sharpens the interpretation of wages.
Total wages at \(\beta=1.120\) sit on the same \(H=4\) rung that defines the
corrected positive-branch prediction \(\betap{4}=1.114\).
GDP and wages therefore occupy the deep-relay side of the ladder. Patents
remain the paradigmatic \(H=2\) innovation observable, whereas inventors
acquire a slightly deeper \(\Heff\approx 2.3\) reflecting co-inventor
coordination beyond the CPC classification route.
That separation is conceptually cleaner than the earlier near-\(H=3\) reading.

% V15: sum-of-power-laws convexity and variance identity (from 18.6).
% Replaces V14 zeta "parabola" overclaim with rigorous convexity statement.
\paragraph{Scope boundary at the 1971 transition.}
The present paper measures the relay-depth ladder within the \(\Omega\)-domain defined by Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} (the \(\Omega\)-series \(\Omega_{\rm competitive\_coop}\), \(\Omega_{\rm territory\_tool}\), \(\Omega_{\rm food\_pre\_irrig}\), \(\Omega_{\rm food\_post\_irrig}\), \(\Omega_{\rm dark\_age}\), \(\Omega_{\rm empire\_writing}\), \(\Omega_{\rm black\_death}\), \(\Omega_{\rm capital\_printing}\),\linebreak \(\Omega_{\rm industry\_science}\), \(\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}\), with \(\Omega\equiv \int N^{2}\,dt\); see Paper~3 SI Appendix S-Phase\linebreak Boundaries). The 1971 boundary spine of this paper corresponds to the Paper~3 \(\Omega_{\rm industry\_science}\to\)\linebreak \(\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}\) transition under the alternate wholesale-adoption interpretation, culminating at the 1971 TFR-peak lock of \(H=5\). Beyond \(\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}\), the \(N^{2}\)-scaling on which \(\Omega\) is built breaks (post-1971 population plateau and AI-substrate amplification \(N\to N_{\rm human}+w_{\rm compute}\,N_{\rm AGI}\)), and the Paper~3 \(\Omega\)-series is no longer the appropriate conceptual framework; Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e} develops the post-\(\Omega\) machinery and is expected to introduce a new integral object distinct from \(\Omega=\int N^{2}\,dt\), since that integral is not extensible across the post-1971 substrate handoff. The cut-off here is therefore not an arbitrary scope rule but the natural span of the Paper~3 \(\Omega\)-domain. Post-1971 substrate-relay phenomena --- including proposed transitions in computational substrates, contemporary digital-economy empirical anchors, and the USPTO inventor-fractional \(\beta\) audit --- are treated in Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e} (the substrate-relay cascade theory) and its Supplementary Information. The USPTO audit is reported there as a non-validation of the previously proposed numerical \(\beta\)-ladder, with the single-population exponent trajectory and the denominator and geography caveats kept separate from cluster-mixture \(H\). Accordingly, no post-1971 \(\beta\)-corridor, \(H=5\to6\) transition, \(H=6\) ladder, AI handoff, or digital-substrate evidence is used in this paper to support the pre-1971 chronology; this paper's scope is exactly the Paper~3 \(\Omega\)-domain.

\subsection{Sum-of-power-laws convexity and variance identity}\label{subsec:sum_power_laws}
Let \(x=\log N\). For any mixed observable with fixed positive coefficients,
\[
Y(N)=\sum_{k} w_k N^{\beta_k}, \qquad \beta_k\equiv \beta(H_k), \qquad w_k>0.
\]
The aggregate is already strictly convex in \(x\), since
\[
\frac{d^2 Y}{d(\log N)^2}=\sum_k w_k \beta_k^2 N^{\beta_k}>0.
\]
The more informative scale-free statement concerns \(F(x)=\log Y(e^x)\). Direct differentiation gives
\begin{equation}
\frac{d^2 \log Y}{d(\log N)^2}=\frac{\sum_k w_k \beta_k^2 N^{\beta_k}}{\sum_j w_j N^{\beta_j}}-\left(\frac{\sum_k w_k \beta_k N^{\beta_k}}{\sum_j w_j N^{\beta_j}}\right)^2>0,
\label{eq:convexity_proof}
\end{equation}
whenever at least two active components have distinct exponents. If we define the induced local weights
\[
q_k(N):=\frac{w_k N^{\beta_k}}{\sum_j w_j N^{\beta_j}},\qquad\bar{\beta}(N):=\sum_k q_k(N)\beta_k,
\]
these \(q_k(N)\) are local output shares and need not coincide with the fixed relay-pathway weights of Eq.~(\ref{eq:mixture}). Equation~(\ref{eq:convexity_proof}) then becomes the variance identity
\begin{equation}
\frac{d^2 \log Y}{d(\log N)^2}=\sum_k q_k(N)\bigl[\beta_k-\bar{\beta}(N)\bigr]^2=: \sigma^2_{\beta|H}(N).
\label{eq:variance_decomp}
\end{equation}
We refer to Eqs.~(\ref{eq:convexity_proof})--(\ref{eq:variance_decomp}) as the sum-of-power-laws theorem. A single power law gives \(\sigma^2_{\beta|H}=0\); heterogeneous relay depths generate positive log--log curvature and thus explain the \(N\)-dependent remainder noted after Eq.~(\ref{eq:mixture}). Over a finite span \([\log N_{\min},\log N_{\max}]\), we summarize this effect by the convexity index
\[
C:=\frac{1}{\log N_{\max}-\log N_{\min}}\int_{\log N_{\min}}^{\log N_{\max}}\frac{d^2\log Y}{d(\log N)^2}\,d(\log N),
\]
which equals the mean slope change per unit \(\log N\). The resulting functional form is convex, but not explicitly quadratic.

% V15: GDP per-capita normalization bridge (from 18.6).
\subsection{GDP per-capita normalization and the bridge to Paper~1}\label{subsec:GDP_normalization_bridge}
Paper~1 and the present paper emphasize different normalizations of the same output. Paper~1 studies per-capita GDP, whereas this paper studies total urban GDP. Writing
\begin{equation}
Y(N,t)=N\,Y_{\mathrm{pc}}(N,t),\qquad\log Y=\log N+\log Y_{\mathrm{pc}},
\label{eq:GDP_decomposition}
\end{equation}
immediately gives
\begin{equation}
\beta(N,t):=\left.\frac{\partial \log Y}{\partial \log N}\right|_{t}=1+\left.\frac{\partial \log Y_{\mathrm{pc}}}{\partial \log N}\right|_{t},\qquad\left.\frac{\partial \log Y}{\partial t}\right|_{N}=\left.\frac{\partial \log Y_{\mathrm{pc}}}{\partial t}\right|_{N}.
\label{eq:per_capita_link}
\end{equation}
The cross-sectional ladder exponent is therefore the extensive baseline \(1\) plus a per-capita correction. At fixed calendar time, contemporary cross-sections usually exhibit only slow size-dependence in \(Y_{\mathrm{pc}}\), so the correction is modest and \(\beta\) remains close to the mixed-observable GDP corridor in Eqs.~(\ref{eq:gdp_nat}) and \eqref{eq:gdp_msa_mean}. Along a longitudinal macro trajectory, by contrast, companion Paper~1 shows that world GDP per capita is curved in the slow variable \(\log N\), namely \(\log Y_{\mathrm{pc}}\propto (\log N)^2\)~\cite{Kato2026a}. No explicit \(t^2\) ansatz is required; temporal curvature appears because \(N=N(t)\) evolves over time. The two papers therefore describe different projections of the same identity: the present paper predicts total-output scaling at fixed \(t\), whereas Paper~1 tracks per-capita curvature along the historical path \(t\mapsto N(t)\). Combined with the convexity identity of Section~\ref{subsec:sum_power_laws}, this yields a unified scaling picture rather than two competing functional forms.

\subsection{Relation to competing urban-scaling frameworks}
The relevant comparison class is the modern urban-scaling toolkit rather than a
single null. Bettencourt's social-reactor program remains the strongest general
benchmark for why interaction-intensive outputs can exceed linearity at all;
Louf--Barthelemy link scaling to commuting geometry and morphology;
Yakubo emphasizes hierarchical network structure; Gomez--Lievano explains the
prevalence and variance of complex urban events; and West's allometric view is
largely orthogonal because it is a size law rather than a theory of
indicator-specific urban exponent selection. The present claim is therefore not
another superlinear fit, but a sparse ladder that places superlinear, linear,
sublinear, and mixed indicators in one framework.

Bettencourt's framework and the present scheme remain complementary rather than reducible. Bettencourt
assigns one common interaction gain $\delta$ to broad output classes, whereas
The ladder assigns indicator-specific relay depths $H_q$ or mixtures thereof. Thus
Bettencourt explains why superlinearity exists, while the relay-depth ladder explains why patents,
wages, deposits, GDP, and infrastructure do not share the same exponent. On the
negative branch, the same relay-depth correction enters with the opposite sign:
interaction-generated outputs amplify with $+\epsH{H}$, whereas support
infrastructure is amortized with $-\epsH{H}$. The result is a mirror-symmetric
account of sublinearity rather than a second unrelated mechanism.

\paragraph{Relation to the Bettencourt 2013 derivation flowchart.}
\citet{Bettencourt2013} derives mean-field scaling exponents
from a small set of geometric axioms: (i) a mixing population; (ii) incremental
network growth; (iii) bounded human effort, $dG/dN=0$; and
(iv) socioeconomic outputs proportional to local social interactions.
These assumptions yield $\beta=1+\delta$ for socioeconomic outputs and
$\beta=1-\delta$ for infrastructural support, with
$\delta=H_{\rm B}/[D(D+H_{\rm B})]$ in $D$ dimensions, where $H_{\rm B}$
denotes the fractal dimension of urban travel paths. We use the subscript
B to distinguish Bettencourt's continuous fractal-dimension $H_{\rm B}$
from the integer relay-depth $H$ of the present ladder; the two parameters
share a symbol but refer to different geometric objects.
In $D=2$ and $H_{\rm B}=1$, the Bettencourt derivation gives
$\delta\simeq 1/6$ and the canonical socioeconomic exponent
$\beta\simeq 7/6\approx 1.167$.
The relay-depth ladder of the present paper is a complementary refinement
of this benchmark rather than a replacement: where the Bettencourt
framework derives \emph{why} cities exceed proportional scaling at all,
the present ladder predicts \emph{which integer rung} a specific
indicator class settles at within that mean-field family.
Numerically, $\beta_+(H{=}3)=1+1/[3\ln 7]\simeq 1.171$ coincides with the
canonical $\beta\simeq 7/6$ within rounding; the canonical socioeconomic
exponent therefore corresponds to $H{=}3$ on the present ladder.

\paragraph{Relation to the Bettencourt 2020 stochastic-growth framework.}
\citet{Bettencourt2020SciAdv} extends the static derivation to a
stochastic-growth setting in which urban agents control net-income volatility
via temporal averaging (consumption smoothing), producing emergent lognormal
statistics for resources and corrections to mean-field scaling whenever the
volatility $\sigma^2(N)$ becomes population-size dependent.
The global wage scaling exponent obtained from 47 years of U.S.\ metropolitan
statistical area data (1969--2016) is reported as
$\beta=1.114$ (95\,\%~CI $[1.111,1.117]$, $R^2=0.935$).
The relay-depth ladder predicts $\beta_+(H{=}4)=1+1/[4\ln 9]\simeq 1.1138$,
which falls within the 95\,\%~CI of this canonical wage panel fit and
locates U.S.\ metropolitan wages at the integer rung $H{=}4$ of the present
ladder. We treat this numerical coincidence as a falsifiable cross-reference
anchor (\S\ref{subsec:other_predictions}, prediction P4) rather than as a
fitted match.
The ladder additionally predicts that the scale-adjusted metropolitan
indicator (SAMI) deviations $\xi_i(t)$ documented by
\citet{Bettencourt2020SciAdv} should decompose by indicator class
along the integer rungs of the ladder rather than collapsing into a single
common $\beta$; the 22-indicator panel closure of
\S\ref{subsec:waterfall_layers} under the $H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster mixture
is consistent with this prediction.

\paragraph{Monograph reference.}
The full canonical urban-scaling framework, comprising both the 2013
mean-field derivation and the 2020 stochastic-growth statistics, is
developed in book-length form in
\cite{Bettencourt2021UrbanScience}.
Throughout this discussion we treat that canonical framework as the
benchmark and the relay-depth ladder as a complementary refinement
that recovers the canonical mean-field exponents at specific integer rungs
($H{=}3$ for $\beta\simeq 7/6$; $H{=}4$ for $\beta\simeq 1.114$) and
predicts indicator-class-specific deviations from any single common
exponent.

\subsection{Other testable predictions}\label{subsec:other_predictions}
Beyond the 22-indicator panel closure that anchors the central claim,
the relay-depth ladder makes five additional families of falsifiable
predictions, each in principle separable from the others.

\paragraph{(P1) Cross-time-beta $H_{\rm era}$ ladder.}
The pre-1971 cross-time exponent ladder developed in
SI~Appendix~S-CrossTimeBeta predicts that historical cross-sectional
exponents measured in restricted time windows track integer
$H_{\rm era}$ rungs rather than the modern single-epoch exponent.
Concretely, the silent-Kramers corridor 1751--1971 is predicted to span
the $H{=}4$ rung ($\beta_+(4)\simeq 1.114$); the late-modern post-1971
onset is predicted to lock at the $H{=}5$ rung
($\beta_+(5)\simeq 1.083$); and the pre-1751
Carolingian/Tang--Song corridor is predicted to occupy the $H{=}3$ rung
($\beta_+(3)\simeq 1.171$). Three pre-registered shift windows
(Materials and Methods) test the predicted boundary years and the
magnitudes of the corresponding rung transitions.

\paragraph{(P2) Size-dependent variance via rung mixture.}
\citet{Bettencourt2020SciAdv} identifies size-dependent
variance $\sigma^2(N)$ as the canonical signature of corrections to
mean-field scaling. The relay-depth ladder predicts a specific structure
for this size dependence: the variance of $\xi_i$ residuals around the
cluster center should decompose as a weighted sum of within-rung
variances at $H\in\{2,3\}$, with the mixture weights $w_H$ tracking
indicator-specific substrate composition rather than entering as free
fit parameters. The 22-indicator panel is consistent with this
prediction under the $H{=}\{2,3\}$ closure (Tier-A-full MAE $=0.017$,
RMSE $=0.045$); a ladder-constrained mixture-of-regressions diagnostic
over the USPTO--CBSA 2010 patent panel (Materials and Methods)
provides an independent narrow check.

\paragraph{(P3) Out-of-sample blind exponents.}
Out-of-sample blind predictions (\S\ref{subsec:waterfall_layers})
for indicator classes not in the canonical Bettencourt 2007 panel are
required to fall within $\pm 0.045$ of the integer ladder rung at the
panel-blind assigned $H$, matching the panel-internal RMSE.
Failure to satisfy this band on a pre-specified blind set falsifies the
ladder's claim to indicator-independent applicability.

\paragraph{(P4) Numerical reconciliation with the canonical mean-field exponents.}
The ladder predicts that the canonical socioeconomic exponent
$\beta\simeq 7/6$~\cite{Bettencourt2013} corresponds to
$\beta_+(H{=}3)$ and that the canonical wage panel exponent
$\beta\simeq 1.114$~\cite{Bettencourt2020SciAdv} corresponds to
$\beta_+(H{=}4)$. Either of these numerical correspondences failing to
fall within the original 95\,\%~CI of the canonical estimate
falsifies the ladder's complementary-refinement claim with respect to
that canonical anchor.

The ladder framework requires (P3) and (P4) for the
complementary-refinement positioning, with (P1)--(P2) extending the
predictive scope under substrate-ledger assumptions developed in
companion manuscripts.

\paragraph{Direct reply to Bettencourt 2007 reviewer-style queries on mechanism and predictions.}
For the two standard reviewer questions (``what is the mechanism, and is it believable?'' and ``what other predictions does it make?''), the present paper offers the following self-contained reply, with theorem derivations referenced to companion papers in preparation. The quantity $(2H+1)^H$ is not a count of agents, messages, firms, or Shannon bits; it is the cardinality of the minimal relay-code space for an ordered $H$-rung coordination traversal, with the signed alphabet $\mathcal{A}_H=\{-H,\dots,-1,0,1,\dots,H\}$ of size $2H+1$ at each rung. The factor $2H+1$ is fixed by the minimal signed alphabet needed at hierarchy depth $H$ ($H$ upstream offsets, $H$ downstream offsets, and one neutral/self relay), and the exponent $H$ comes from composing exactly one such relay decision at each of the $H$ rungs of a full traversal, so the code space is $\mathcal{A}_H^{\times H}$. Alternative formulas such as $(3H+2)^H$ or $(2H+1)^{H+1}$ would add extra alphabet symbols or an extra relay slot not required by the structural model, so they are rejected by minimality rather than by curve fitting. Empirically, the primary observable is the predicted exponent $\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$, while the code volume itself can only be checked indirectly through coordination protocol or relay-motif diversity when suitable microdata exist; this distinguishes the present claim from a direct census-count proposal. The four remaining predictions (P1)--(P4) above (cross-time-$\beta$ ladder, size-dependent variance, out-of-sample blind exponents, numerical reconciliation with canonical mean-field exponents) supply additional falsifiable consequences orthogonal to the 22-panel anchor itself; the mechanism and the predictions together address the two standard reviewer queries within a single complementary-refinement framework anchored on the Bettencourt 22-indicator panel.


\subsection{Cross-branch balancing and the linear class}
\label{subsec:cross_branch_balance}
The five near-linear indicators in Table~\textsf{S-PrimaryPanelTable} are more
naturally explained by finite-depth cross-branch balance than by the formal
$H\to\infty$ limit. Write a near-linear observable as
\begin{equation}
\beff=\pi_{+}\,\betap{H}+\pi_{-}\,\betam{H}
    =1+(\pi_{+}-\pi_{-})\,\epsH{H},
\qquad \pi_{+}+\pi_{-}=1.
\label{eq:same_depth_balance}
\end{equation}
When the generation and coverage shares nearly balance, the anomalous
correction cancels and $\beta\approx 1$ at finite relay depth.
Equivalently, introducing the generation--coverage asymmetry
$\sigma_{gc}:=\pi_{+}-\pi_{-}\in[-1,1]$, the effective exponent reads
$\beff=1+\sigma_{gc}\,\epsH{H}$, which vanishes exactly at $\sigma_{gc}=0$
(linear attractor).  A formal treatment of this generation--coverage duality
and its cross-branch balance interpretation is given in
SI~Section~\textsf{S-sigma-gc-duality}.

% V38: π_+^* unified to 0.50 for same-depth relay-level mixture (K9_10.7r4 fix #2).
% The formula β_eff = 1 + (π_+ − π_−)ε(H) gives β_eff=1 exactly at π_+=π_-=1/2.
This interpretation has three advantages. It avoids the physically implausible
infinite-chain reading, explains why near-linear observables cluster tightly
around $\beta=1$, and predicts that decomposition should reveal offsetting
superlinear and sublinear components. For the same-depth relay-level mixture
in Eq.~(\ref{subsec:cross_branch_balance}), the exact balance point is
$\pi_{+}=\pi_{-}=1/2$. The near-linear rows should therefore be read as
finite-depth cross-branch balances, with only modest deviations from
$1/2$ tolerated by the reported confidence intervals.
