\subsection{From intuitive rungs to network-anchored relay depth}\label{subsec:network_anchored_relay}
Earlier drafts assigned relay depth largely by functional intuition. The
network-anchored rule below replaces that procedure. Relay
depth $H$ is not reducible to any single network statistic: average
shortest-path length, degree-distribution exponent, and modularity each capture
only part of relay structure. The empirical protocol is therefore two-stage.
% V38: \Heff definition unified as derived coordinate (K9_10.7r4 fix #1).
When independent structural evidence exists, we assign integer relay depths
$H_k$ or mixture weights $\pi_k$ before opening $\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}$.
The reported continuous $\Heff$ is then the derived coordinate obtained from
$\epsH{\Heff}=\sum_k \pi_k\,\epsH{H_k}$; it is not a primitive measured depth.
Only rows without such evidence retain an integer rung as a provisional display prior.

\paragraph{Branch and relay-depth registry: $\beta$-independent assignment.}
For each indicator, the branch sign $\sigma\in\{+,-\}$ and the integer
relay depth $H$ (or mixture support) are derived from two pre-$\beta$
network features: the indicator's coordination network type
(\textit{physical infrastructure}, \textit{socio-economic coordination},
or \textit{hybrid}) and its substrate constraint (\textit{area bounded},
\textit{volume bounded}, or \textit{unbounded densification}).
The derivation rule is structural rather than statistical: an
area/volume-constrained physical-infrastructure network maps to
$\beta_{-}$, an unbounded-densification socio-economic network maps to
$\beta_{+}$, and hybrid cases (such as
electricity consumption) are flagged for expert review with a
documented basis. This protocol is retrospective for the present
22-panel anchor but is committed to a frozen public registry in a
companion data package for forward indicator classes; full provenance
columns---indicator name, coordination network description, branch
basis, $H$/mix basis, and assignment date---are tabulated in the SI
Appendix~\ref{sec:S-PanelOrigins}, and a structured machine-readable
form is planned for the supplementary release.

Three anchors are now objective rather than intuitive. Patents remain in the
$H\approx 2$ innovation class, total wages are anchored at $H\approx 4$,
and GDP is a deep-relay mixture with
$\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}\approx 4.42$ and
$\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}\approx 4.02$. The same mixture logic resolves
the $H=2\leftrightarrow 3$ crossover valley on both branches: gasoline
stations and gasoline sales occupy a negative-branch mixture of
$\beta_{-}(2)$ and $\beta_{-}(3)$, while patents and inventors are
positive-branch mixtures of $\betap{2}$ and $\betap{3}$. With these
same-branch composition corrections the panel rises from $17/22$ to
$21/22$ CI coverage, and the continuous-$\Heff$ row provides a
diagnostic refinement at the same $21/22$ level.  The full $22/22$
closure is reached via the hybrid label-free protocol of
Sec.~\ref{subsec:waterfall_layers}: the fixed $H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster
integer mixture anchors the crossover-valley bulk, while the same
zero-fitted-exponent $\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)$ interpolant accommodates the
remaining outlier indicators. Neither layer fits an indicator-specific
exponent.

% V38: "measured H_eff" → "derived H_eff" for consistency (K9_10.7r4 fix #1).
The resulting rule is simple. Use the derived $\Heff$ when the
observable identity is direct and structural weights $\pi_k$ are available; use a
mixture when the evidence indicates crossover or deep-relay composition; and
retain integer $H$ as a display class for uncovered rows. Independent support
for this reading comes from the four-route $H$-measurement program summarized
in the SI, where structurally distinct routes converge on the same
indicator-specific relay assignments.

\subsection{Future Work: Conjecture: Self-organized H from network topology}
\label{subsec:H_selforg_conjecture}
A natural next question is whether relay depth $H$ can itself be recovered
from network topology rather than from external labels or independently measured
mixtures. We frame that possibility as a conjecture, not as a result of the
present paper. The current evidence supports network-anchored assignment and
mixture measurement, but not a unique graph-to-$H$ inversion. The appropriate
future task is therefore to test whether controlled multilayer networks and
observable-specific urban interaction graphs can recover the same relay-depth
structure without post hoc labeling.

\subsection{City-definition sensitivity as \(\Heff\) variation}
Boundary sensitivity does not imply that the ladder itself is unstable. It
implies that raw exponents are invariant only conditionally on the measurement
frame and on the mixture weights implied by that frame. If an observable is a
same-branch mixture, then changing the city definition reweights $\pi_k(D)$
and therefore changes the derived coordinate $\Heff(D)$. Arcaute-style
threshold sweeps can thus be recast as $\Heff$ sweeps: broader definitions
move $\beta$ toward $1$, narrower definitions move $|\beta-1|$ away from
zero, and the relevant invariant is the relay-depth corridor rather than one
unconditional slope.

\subsection{Relation to network-science metrics}
Relay depth $H$ is a mesoscopic structural parameter, not a single network
statistic. No model-independent formula maps $H$ uniquely to the degree
exponent, mean path length, or modularity of an urban interaction network.
Those observables can constrain relay structure, but only through an explicit
closure and measurement protocol. The practical implication is straightforward:
validating $H$ from network data requires observable-specific proxies rather
than one universal graph-theoretic shortcut.

% V53: expanded to 7-paragraph scope-limit structure from K9_118.9 Q6.1
% (wave59 K9_118 batch). Preempts 12-attack audit by separating assignment
% vs exponent map, flagging continuous H_eff as secondary, acknowledging
% small-panel constraints, and stating explicit falsification conditions.
\subsection{Anticipated objections and scope limits}\label{subsec:anticipated_objections}

Several objections are natural for a zero-fitted-exponent exponent-selection claim,
and the strongest version of the manuscript is obtained by stating them
explicitly.

\paragraph{Relay depth is not fitted after observing the slope.}
The theory would be circular if \(H\) were adjusted to fit
\(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}\) and then declared predictive.  We therefore separate
the exponent map from the assignment problem.  The map
\(\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\) has no fitted coefficient once \(H\) is
specified.  The assignment of \(H\), however, is an empirical structural task.
For that reason the SI distinguishes structural routes (CPC composition,
input--output layering, occupational structure, and network topology) from
model-based audit routes such as ML and BIC.  Only the former are treated as
anti-circular evidence; the latter are diagnostics.  An alternative
\(\epsilon\) function (Alt2: \(\epsilon_{\mathrm{alt}}=1/(H^{2}\ln H)\)) is
rejected by the data (\(\Delta\mathrm{AIC}=+28.7\), likelihood-ratio
\(p=0.021\)), confirming that the functional form is empirically constrained,
not merely convenient.

\paragraph{Continuous effective depth is secondary.}
The primary test is the integer confrontation: \(17/22\) reported confidence
intervals contain the integer ladder prediction.  Continuous \(\Heff\) is not a
new primitive rung and is not used as an unrestricted inverse fit.  It is a
derived coordinate for predeclared mixture or crossover cases, with
\(\epsilon(\Heff)=\sum_k\pi_k\,\epsilon(H_k)\).  Composition corrections raise
the coverage to \(21/22\), and the final continuous row is reported as a
diagnostic refinement rather than as the main endpoint.  A paired
McNemar-style accounting of the \(17/22\to 21/22\) improvement gives four
No\(\to\)Yes changes and no Yes\(\to\)No changes; because the discordant count
is small, this is reported descriptively rather than as a decisive
significance claim.

\paragraph{The 22-indicator panel is small but stress-tested.}
The Bettencourt panel is retained because it is the canonical multi-indicator
urban-scaling benchmark, not because it is sufficient by itself.  The SI
therefore reports leave-one-out stability, repeated 5-fold resampling,
domain-block bootstrap, ICC-adjusted effective sample size, hierarchical
residual checks, and a permutation test that randomly reassigns ladder-rung
assignments to indicators.  These analyses do not turn \(n=22\) into a
large sample.  They support the narrower claim that the canonical-panel
pattern is not a broad-interval, one-domain, or random-relabeling artifact.

\paragraph{The benchmark is supplemented by newer and external checks.}
The paper does not rely only on the original 2007 panel.  Patent scaling is
stable across independent 2001 and 2010 MSA slices; the 2010 CPC section test
uses patent-domain structure rather than a rebinned Bettencourt row; and
additional checks include international GDP and patent frames, Google Places
amenities, and waste/emissions indicators.  These checks are not a complete
preregistered train/test replication of all 22 original indicators.  They are
reported as external transportability tests of the same exponent-selection
logic.

\paragraph{Boundary sensitivity is incorporated, not denied.}
Raw urban exponents move when the city definition, commuting field, or
aggregation frame changes.  The invariant object in this manuscript is
therefore conditional: a relay-depth corridor after the measurement frame and
mixture weights have been specified.  The SI separates European FUA-pooled
GDP from the LUZ GDP benchmark, distinguishes national and metropolitan GDP
coordinates, and treats Japan GDP as a boundary-definition stress test rather
than a hidden success.  A row is eligible for the primary score only when its
measurement frame is comparable to the frame used for its structural
assignment.

\paragraph{Relation to existing urban-scaling theory.}
Bettencourt's social-reactor theory remains the baseline for why
interaction-intensive outputs can exceed linearity at all
\citep{Bettencourt2007,Bettencourt2013}.  The present contribution is not a
replacement of that mechanism.  It is an observable-specific selector for why
patents, inventors, wages, GDP, deposits, electricity, roads, housing, and
gasoline occupy different superlinear, near-linear, or sublinear positions on
one mirror-symmetric ladder.  Likewise, the biological comparison is a scope
extension under explicit structural conditions, not evidence that every
dissipative system obeys the ladder.

\paragraph{What would falsify the framework.}
The framework would be challenged by independently measured relay depths
that systematically contradict the assigned rungs, out-of-sample panels
whose indicator-specific depths miss the ladder predictions by large margins,
failure to recover offsetting generation and coverage components in
near-linear rows, or boundary-harmonized international panels that fall
outside the stated relay-depth corridors.  These are domain-conditioned
tests, not generic claims that one unconditional slope is invariant across
every city definition.

\subsection{Falsifiability, identification, and limits}
The framework is only interesting if it can fail. The present evidence is
encouraging---the primary integer-rung test gives $17/22$, same-branch
sublinear composition gives $19/22$, continuous $\Heff$ provides a
secondary sensitivity coordinate at $21/22$, and the central $22/22$
closure is reached via the fixed hybrid label-free protocol: the
$H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster anchors the crossover-valley bulk, while the
same zero-fitted-exponent $\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)$ interpolant accommodates
outlier indicators (no indicator-specific exponent fitting); the panel-level diagnostics are
$\mathrm{MAE}=0.017$ (Tier-A-full), $\mathrm{RMSE}=0.030$, a $4/4$ grouped CPC blind
test, and a $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}=+48$ advantage over a Gomez--Lievano-type
comparison---but these numbers matter
mainly because they sharpen rejection conditions rather than replace them.

Within the intended relay domain, the theory would be directly challenged by
any of the following: repeated estimates outside the ladder bounds
$[\betam{1},\betap{1}]$; independently measured relay depth that
systematically contradicts the assigned rung; out-of-sample settings with weak
predictive content; structural depth estimates that miss the ladder predictions
by large margins; or large secular drift unexplained by changing mixture
weights. These tests must be applied within coherent domains and within one
branch at a time, since pooling positive- and negative-branch observables can
create spurious self-falsifications.

Identification is the key scope condition. If one inspects
$\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}$ before assigning $H$, the ladder degenerates into a
relabeling scheme. The protocol must run in the opposite order: measure
$H$, map it to $\beta_{\mathrm{pred}}$, and only then open the observed
slope. The same logic extends to mixtures: when the component-signature matrix
fails the rank condition, multiple latent decompositions generate the same
aggregate exponent, so $\Heff$ remains a descriptive coordinate but the
underlying mixture is not unique. Some assignments therefore remain partly
theory-guided, especially near $\beta=1$, where high-$H$ inversion is
compressed. The SI makes these limits explicit rather than hiding them.

\subsection{International generalizability}
The ladder is not intended as a U.S.-specific artifact. Country-by-country OLS
fits on OECD functional urban area data show substantial cross-country
variation in $\beta$ but consistent rung alignment: Poland
($\bar\beta=1.307$) matches $\betap{2}=1.311$ to within $0.004$, the
Netherlands ($\bar\beta=1.173$) matches $\betap{3}=1.171$ to within
$0.002$, and mature service economies such as the United Kingdom and Italy
sit near deep-relay $\Heff$ values around $10$--$12$. The Netherlands
also shows near-zero temporal drift.

More broadly, the non-U.S.\ GDP checks reported here place 10 of 11
independently sourced entries inside the corresponding ladder corridor; the lone
miss is the most restrictive Japanese GDP definition. The right interpretation
is conditional transportability: the framework survives frame shifts when the
observable identity is preserved and the measurement frame is made explicit.

% V36: Biological scaling subsection (from K9_4.7r1, 5.2r1, 5.3r1, 5.5r1, 5.6r1)
\subsection{Biological scaling as a special case}\label{subsec:biological_scaling}
The relay-depth ladder is not inherently urban. West, Brown, and Enquist
(WBE) derived allometric exponents from space-filling fractal networks with
branching dimension~$d$, yielding $\beta=d/(d+1)$. This form is a strict
subset of the ladder's negative branch: setting
$d=H_{\mathrm{eff}}\ln(2H_{\mathrm{eff}}+1)-1$ recovers the WBE family exactly
on $\beta_{-}(H_{\mathrm{eff}})$ and never on $\beta_{+}(H)$. Kleiber's
empirical $\beta\approx 3/4$ is therefore realized \emph{exclusively on the
negative branch}, with $H_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 2.315$, and can be represented
to integer-rung accuracy by a two-component mixture of $H=2$ ($56.5\%$) and
$H=3$ ($43.5\%$) relay pathways; it is not a positive-branch $H=3$
assignment. Rubner's competing $\beta\approx 2/3$ corresponds to pure $H=2$
on the same negative branch. Insect-colony metabolic scaling at
$\beta\approx 0.813\approx\beta_{-}(3)$ likewise remains on the negative
branch, placing superorganisms on the same $H=3$ rung, with relay depth
reflecting the trophallaxis network depth of the colony. Physarum
polycephalum (slime-mold) transport networks yield $H\approx 2$ when
evaluated via directed Kirchhoff index, consistent with a single-relay
tubular architecture. These examples suggest that the
integer relay ladder, originally motivated by urban production networks, may
serve as a broader organizing principle for hierarchically structured
output-generating systems, with the relay-depth ladder subsuming WBE as a special case
% V38: S11 → \ref (K9_10.7r4 fix #3).
(detailed in the companion Paper 5).

% V51: Dimensionality conjecture (exploratory corollary, from 3D clustering sim).
\subsection{Dimensionality conjecture (exploratory)}\label{subsec:dim_conjecture}
As an exploratory corollary, the empirical 2D~$\to$~3D clustering progression
(population--patents supporting $k=2$ by BIC, and
population--patents--GDP supporting $k=3$ by BIC) motivates a dimensionality
conjecture: for $k$ distinct integer-$H$ regimes, a feature set of
dimension $d\geq k$ satisfying full affine rank on the theoretical slope
vectors can, in principle, recover the regimes at sufficient sample size.
We formalize this hypothesis conditionally in SI
Section~\textsf{S-dim-conjecture} and propose testing it via curated 4D/5D
panels (SI~Section~\textsf{S-dim-4D5D-design}). An effective-rank corollary
bounding the empirically resolvable $k$ by the observable civilization stage
is discussed in the companion Paper 5.

\subsection{Conclusion}

This paper asked whether urban scaling exponents can be predicted rather than
freely fitted.
A discrete relay-depth law,
\(\epsH{H}=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\), generates a zero-fitted-exponent ladder that matches
\(17/22\) canonical Bettencourt indicators at strict integer resolution.
Same-branch sublinear composition raises this to \(19/22\); continuous
\(\Heff\) gives a secondary sensitivity coordinate at \(21/22\); and the
\(22/22\) closure is obtained via a hybrid label-free protocol in which
the fixed \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) cluster integer mixture anchors the central
crossover-valley bulk and the same zero-fitted-exponent
\(\beta_{\pm}(\Heff)\) interpolant accommodates outlier indicators. Neither
layer fits an indicator-specific exponent once the mixture weights
\(\pi_j\) and the cluster-assignment algorithm are pre-registered.
Panel-level diagnostics attain \(\mathrm{MAE}=0.017\) on Tier-A-full (and $0.015$ on the all-22 disclosed panel), and the result
survives four explicit null-model confrontations.
The correction of the GDP anchor sharpens the theory rather than weakening it:
the correct reading is an \(H=4\)--5 corridor, with
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}=1.099\)
(\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,MSA\text{-}mean}}\approx 4.42\)) and
\(\beff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}=1.113\)
(\(\Heff^{\mathrm{GDP,national}}\approx 4.02\)),
while total wages sit directly on the \(H=4\) rung.
The European GDP benchmark in LUZ space remains compatible with that broader
deep-relay interpretation.

The contribution is not merely another superlinear regression; it is a single scaffold that places superlinear, linear, sublinear, and mixed
indicators on one mirror-symmetric ladder and makes composition itself part of
the theory.
A structural bonus is the sum-of-power-laws theorem
(Section~\ref{subsec:sum_power_laws}): any mixed observable whose sectors
carry distinct relay depths exhibits positive log--log
curvature through the identity
\[
\frac{d^2 \log Y}{d(\log N)^2}=\sigma^2_{\beta|H}(N)>0,
\]
even when every relay depth is time-invariant. This provides a bridge between the
cross-sectional scaling law derived here and the longitudinal convexity documented
independently in Paper~1~\cite{Kato2026a}. The operator-level realization of that
bridge, in which the composition-current intensity is identified with a
slice-operator commutator on the composite field
$T_{\mathrm{eff}}(t,n)=n\,\tau(t,n)$ and the Paper~1 parabolic coefficient
$1/d^{2}\simeq 0.18559$ (equivalently, derivative coefficient $2/d^{2}\simeq 0.37118$) is locked non-perturbatively, is given in Companion
Paper~5 (SI~\S\,S-LCB)~\cite{Kato2026e}.
That bridge may matter beyond the present panel: if the sum-of-power-laws theorem implies longitudinal convexity under time-invariant relay depths, then the same structural mixture logic can connect the convex world-GDP relation in Paper~1, the population-saturation mechanisms developed in Papers~2 and~3, and, together, a constrained forecast problem in which GDP growth bends predictably once population approaches a ceiling even without any discrete sectoral change in \(H\)~\cite{Kato2026a,Kato2026b,Kato2026c}.
If non-human agents become economically central, they would introduce a distinct relay-depth composition rather than simply extend the human ladder, so human- and machine-generated GDP could in principle scale as partially separate aggregates.
The decisive move is from continuous slope estimation to discrete structural
classification plus externally measurable mixtures.
For that reason, the present manuscript is best read as a proposal for how
urban scaling should be falsified:
it reduces the empirical question from ``what slope fits this indicator?'' to
``what relay depth, or what measured mixture of depths, generated this
indicator?''

% V14 epsilon: future directions (from 15.8 COVID + 15.9 fintech evaluations).
Several extensions follow naturally.
First, regime transitions---whether from pandemic-induced remote-work shifts
or from sectoral maturation in emerging industries---should manifest as
transient changes in \(\Heff\) rather than as permanent departures from the
ladder.
Second, the input--output upstreamness measure provides a complementary route
to \(H\) that can be estimated from BEA supply-use tables without any
network-topology assumption (see companion Paper 3 SI).
Third, an information-theoretic interpretation of \(\epsH{H}\) as the
inverse serial relay log-cardinality may provide a deeper foundation for the
\(2H+1\) state-count, connecting the framework to channel-capacity arguments
in organizational theory.
A complementary thermodynamic argument (SI~Section~\textsf{S-free-energy-uniqueness})
shows that $H$ is also uniquely selected by free-energy minimization, provided
the network parameters $(\Lambda_G,\Gamma_G)$ are known.
Under explicit uniform-traffic / stage-equipartition / homogeneous-maintenance
assumptions, both coefficients are now derived microscopically from graph
invariants: $\Lambda_G=c_\Lambda\,\mathrm{Kf}(G^{\leftrightarrow})$ is an
effective-resistance relay-complexity burden
(SI~Section~\textsf{S-Lambda-G-microfoundation}), and
$\Gamma_G=c_\Gamma\,\rho_E(G)$ is a density-normalized active-edge maintenance
cost (SI~Section~\textsf{S-Gamma-G-microfoundation}).
Together they yield a BEA 71-sector prediction
$H^{\ast}\approx 4.18$ that agrees with the independently measured
GDP corridor $H_{\mathrm{eff}}\in[4.02,4.42]$, removing $(\Lambda_G,\Gamma_G)$
from the list of free phenomenological parameters and making the selector
$F_G(H;T)$ reduces fitted-parameter freedom for the BEA graph test; under explicit assumptions $\Lambda_G$ and $\Gamma_G$ are obtained from graph invariants, but fully parameter-free status remains a target for future work (cf.\ open conditions on anchor-dependent calibration).
We note two important boundary results:
a linear-in-time relay trajectory $H(t)$ cannot reproduce the
longitudinal parabolic regularity of Paper~1
(SI~Section~\textsf{S-impossibility-linear-H}), underscoring the need for
an endogenous sector-weight evolution law---this negative result is
complemented by the positive operator-level identification in Companion
Paper~5 (SI~\S\,S-LCB) that locks the parabola slope at $2/d^{2}$ through
the ergodicity-gap composition current rather than through any explicit
$H(t)$ trajectory~\cite{Kato2026e};
and $\beta\to 1$ at $H\to\infty$ is a \emph{decoupling} limit, not an
extinction singularity (SI~Section~\textsf{S-beta-one-limit}).
Fourth, endogenous relay-depth determination via community detection or
spectral methods on urban interaction networks
(Section~\ref{subsec:H_selforg_conjecture}) could eliminate the need for external
categorical labels entirely, making the framework self-contained.
A preliminary result in this direction is the network
renormalization-group derivation
(SI~Section~\textsf{S-network-RG-H}), which shows that both $H$ and
the factor $\ln(2H+1)$ can emerge from iterative coarse-graining of
the production network without any external label assignment.

Fifth, and most broadly, the relay-depth correction
$\epsH{H}=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ is not intrinsically urban.
The derivation rests on two ingredients only: a hierarchical topology
with integer depth $H$, and a free-energy balance between
communication cost ($\Lambda_G/H$) and wiring cost ($\Gamma_G\cdot H$).
Any dissipative system that self-organizes into a
topological hierarchy---whether a biological vascular network, an
insect colony, or a slime-mold transport mesh---satisfies both
ingredients and should therefore obey the same
$\beta=1\pm\epsH{H}$ ladder.
The composition rule $\beff=\sum_k\pi_k\,\beta(H_k)$
then predicts that Kleiber's three-quarter-power metabolic
scaling~\cite{Kleiber1932,West1997} corresponds \emph{exclusively} to a
negative-branch mixture of $H=2$ and $H=3$ subsystems
($\pi_2\approx 0.565$, $\pi_3\approx 0.435$), with
$\Heff\approx 2.315$; the same numerical value must not be re-read as a
positive-branch $H=3$ assignment. This is a testable prediction that can be
checked against measured hierarchy distributions in mammalian vascular and
respiratory networks.
More generally, West--Brown--Enquist spatial-dimension exponents
$\beta=d/(d+1)$ map one-to-one onto negative-branch effective relay depths,
with $d=3$ giving $\Heff\approx 2.315$, so the ladder subsumes
the space-filling-network program as a special case of hierarchical
composition.
If confirmed, this correspondence would unify urban and biological
allometry under a single dissipative-hierarchy framework.

% V36: Scope and temporal implications (from K9_6.5r1, 6.6, 6.7r1)
\paragraph{Scope and temporal implications.}
The present validation covers OECD, EU, Chinese, and Japanese cities;
extension to low-income contexts (e.g.\ Sub-Saharan Africa) awaits
city-level GDP data with sufficient geographic coverage.
Because $\beta^{+}(H)$ is monotonically decreasing in~$H$, the
secular trend toward $\beta\!\approx\!1$ in aggregate GDP reflects
deepening relay depth via composition shift~$\pi_k(t)$, not
convergence to a trivial $H\!\to\!\infty$ limit.
Similarly, a pandemic-induced decrease in~$\beta$ would imply
relay-depth increase or composition reweighting, not relay collapse---a
prediction testable with pre- and post-COVID urban panels.

% V41: Δ → Δ_S rename + Theorem 2 (K9_13.5r1 H=1 ⇔ p=2 identity).
% Notation sync with P3 V42 (Δ_ceil = 1 − ε(H) used in P3; Δ_S = 1/H − ε(H) here).
\paragraph{Temporal--spatial identity (Theorem 2).}
The von~Foerster exponent $p=2$ (aggregate population growth via pairwise
interaction) and the relay-depth exponent $\betap{1}=1+1/\ln 3 \approx 1.910$
are related by a structural identity up to entropy renormalization:
$p=2$ is the temporal growth engine, whereas $\betap{1}$ is the
cross-sectional spatial projection of that engine through a one-step relay.

\begin{theorem}[Entropy-discounted pairwise identity; proof in SI~\textsf{S-H1-vonFoerster-identity}]
Within the ladder $\betap{H}=1+\epsH{H}$ with the primitive
$\epsH{H}=1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$, the minimal positive rung $H=1$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
\betap{1}=2-\DS(1),\qquad \DS(1)=1-\frac{1}{\ln 3}\approx 0.0898,
\label{eq:H1_p2_identity}
\end{equation}
where $\DS(H):= 1/H-\epsH{H}=(1/H)[1-1/\ln(2H+1)]$ is the per-rung
entropy cost of embedding the pairwise interaction into a serial relay.
\end{theorem}

The quantity $\DS(H)$ differs from the ceiling gap $\Dceil(H):=
p-\betap{H}=1-\epsH{H}$ used in the companion paper~\cite{Kato2026c} by
\begin{equation}
\Dceil(H)-\DS(H)=\frac{H-1}{H},
\label{eq:Dceil_DS_identity}
\end{equation}
and the two coincide at $H=1$.  $\DS$ decreases monotonically on integer
rungs $H\ge 2$ (Appendix~\textsf{S-Delta-S-properties}) and vanishes as
$H\to\infty$; its $H=1$ value $0.0898$ is the entropy discount paid when
the full $N^{2}$ pairwise engine is mediated by the shallowest possible
relay.  A companion paper~\cite{Kato2026c} develops the population-dynamics
implications of this correspondence in detail.

\paragraph{General-$H$ bridge formula (Theorem 2.1).}
The $H=1$ identity~\eqref{eq:H1_p2_identity} extends to all integer $H\ge 1$
as a clean two-loss decomposition between the unrenormalized pairwise
exponent $p=2$ and the achieved ladder rung:

\begin{theorem}[General $H$ pairwise relay-depth bridge; proof in the companion Paper 3 SI]
For every $H\in\mathbb{N}_{\ge 1}$,
\begin{equation}
\betap{H}\;=\;2\;-\;\DS(H)\;-\;\frac{H-1}{H},
\label{eq:general_bridge}
\end{equation}
where the first loss $\DS(H)=(1/H)[1-1/\ln(2H+1)]$ is the per-rung entropy
discount intrinsic to embedding the pairwise interaction into a serial relay
of any depth, and the second loss $(H-1)/H$ is the extra dilution that
appears only at $H>1$.  At $H=1$ the second loss vanishes and~\eqref{eq:general_bridge}
collapses to~\eqref{eq:H1_p2_identity}.
\end{theorem}

The decomposition makes the structural origin of the $\betap{H}\to 1$ limit
transparent: as $H\to\infty$, $\DS(H)\to 0$ and $(H-1)/H\to 1$, so the gap
to the pairwise ceiling $p=2$ approaches $1$, i.e.\ the ladder exponent
approaches the linear baseline.  Conversely, the deepest superlinear excess
is realized at $H=1$, where only the entropy discount applies.  The companion
paper~\cite{Kato2026c} shows that the same decomposition controls the
temporal-side projection: once the mixture is frozen, the finite-difference
substitute for the cross-sectional equation reduces to an identity, closing
the ergodicity gap as an ergodic-bridge theorem.

\subsection{Project placement}

The present paper is the multi-indicator validation layer for the
relay-depth ladder framework. Companion preprints in preparation~\cite{Kato2026a,Kato2026b,Kato2026c}
develop the world GDP-per-capita macro relation, demographic-transition
chain, and exogenous-ceiling population-collapse model that motivate the
current relay-depth program.
The explicit ergodic-bridge theorem for the temporal projection under frozen
composition and $\dot H = 0$, closing the cross-sectional/longitudinal
identification, is now supplied by the companion Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e}:
its SI~\S\,S-LCB derives an operator-level longitudinal--cross-sectional
bridge that identifies the composition-current intensity
$\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{eg}}(x)$ with the commutator of two slice operators
acting on the composite field $T_{\mathrm{eff}}(t,n)=n\,\tau(t,n)$, and
thereby locks the Paper~1 parabolic coefficient at $1/d^{2}\simeq 0.18559$ (equivalently, derivative coefficient $2/d^{2}\simeq 0.37118$). A
cross-paper consistency audit of the $T_{\mathrm{eff}}$ family across
Papers~1--5---comprising a definition matrix, an inconsistency census with
recommended fixes, a four-rung bootstrap numerical cross-check, and three
formal lemmas---is given in SI~\S\,S-CC of the same paper.
The throughput identification that upgrades the rank-$3$ thermodynamic closure
to a conditional rank-$4$ closure (via a single primitive stage clock
$\nu_0$) is developed in Section~\textsf{S-throughput-nu-identification} of the
SI.
Those companion papers motivate the current relay-depth program but do not
supply free parameters for the 22-indicator ladder confrontation itself.

% V58 (2026-05-02, wave67b, C^3 feedback bundle): sensitivity-layer
% coexistence paragraph distinguishes the discrete cluster integer mixture
% central claim (22/22, fitted-parameter free) from the aggregate
% continuous H_eff sensitivity layer (21/22). Reviewer-defense minimal
% diff under integrate condition (b); no new ladder rung, no new theorem.
% V59 (2026-05-02, wave67c, forward-cite freeze): book in-preparation
% reference removed; coexistence statement kept self-contained because
% the layer distinction is internally valid without an external pointer.
\paragraph{Hybrid framework: \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) cluster anchors bulk, continuous \(H_{\mathrm{eff}}\) accommodates outliers.}
The central claim of this paper is hybrid: the label-free 2-component
integer-\(H\) cluster mixture with \(H\in\{2,3\}\) and physical
dimensionality \(d=3\) anchors the bulk of the Bettencourt panel
structurally (which two relay depths are physically active for $d{=}3$
urban carriers), while the continuous \(\beta_{\pm}(H_{\mathrm{eff}})\)
interpolant evaluated at fractional depth accommodates the small set of
outlier indicators that sit between integer rungs (e.g.\
\(\beta=1.113\to H_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 4.02\) for national GDP and
\(\beta=1.099\to H_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 4.42\) for MSA-average GDP).
Neither layer introduces an indicator-specific fitted exponent: both rest
on the same zero-fitted-exponent ladder \(\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\),
with the continuous-\(H_{\mathrm{eff}}\) layer being that ladder
evaluated at fractional \(H\) rather than a free indicator-by-indicator
fit. The two layers---cluster integer structural anchor and continuous
\(H_{\mathrm{eff}}\) outlier accommodation---coexist consistently within
the same relay-depth ladder framework and satisfy
\(\epsilon(H_{\mathrm{eff}})=\sum_k w_k\,\epsilon(H_k)\) on a same-branch
mixture. They are different reductions of the same underlying
\(\sum_h w_h\beta_{\pm}(h)\) object; the cluster integer mixture supplies
the identification of active relay depths, and the continuous
\(H_{\mathrm{eff}}\) supplies the aggregate-level coordinate needed for
outlier and cross-paper comparison.

\paragraph{$H_{\rm era}$ as a structural cap on $H_{\rm obs}$ (cross-paper bridge).}
The civilisational regime depth \(H_{\rm era}\) is used here only as a support condition on observable-level relay depths, not as a second estimator of the Bettencourt exponents. Under the support-boundedness assumption stated in the Results (\(H_{\rm obs}\leq H_{\rm era}\) at stationary regime, with temporary support up to \(H_{\rm era}+1\) during an active adjacent transition), non-adjacent support is outside the present paper's scoring rule. This bridge is invoked only to justify why a cross-sectional urban panel may contain low-\(H_{\rm obs}\) innovation rows together with GDP/wage-class \(H_{\rm obs}\approx4\) rows. The historical spine retained here is limited to three orientation boundaries: AD~151, the 1820 industrial-onset entry, and the 1971 \(H_{\rm era}=4\to5\) terminal lock (TFR-peak) under the Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} alternative wholesale-adoption reading. These dates are not used as cross-time \(\beta\) observations and do not supply fitted exponents for the 22-panel. Cross-time \(\beta\) reconstructions and all post-1971 substrate-relay claims are deferred to Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e} and Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} SI; the Bettencourt benchmark remains a single-epoch cross-sectional exponent test of \(H_{\rm obs}\) and its mixtures.

\paragraph{Companion preprints.}
Companion manuscripts in preparation, on related topics in urban scaling, growth dynamics, and substrate-relay phenomena, are not required for the present 22-panel test. They are mentioned here only for cross-paper orientation and will be released separately when available. The present 22-panel cross-sectional test is self-contained and does not depend on the companion manuscripts.

% V53: new Materials and Methods section (wave59 K9_118.9 Q6.3). Five
% one-paragraph clarifications that preempt post-hoc fitting concerns by
% stating assignment order, endpoint structure, measurement-frame
% conditioning, continuous-depth status, and the outlier-gate rule.
\paragraph{H-formation acceleration conjecture (formal test deferred to Paper~11).}
Let $t_H$ denote the latent boundary time at which the $H$-era of relay depth $H$ gives rise to the next era, and let $\Delta_H = t_{H+1}-t_H$. The $H_{\rm era}$ ledger maintained in companion Paper~11 (in preparation) suggests that $\log_{10}\Delta_H$ decreases approximately linearly in $H$, i.e.\ $\Delta_H \approx A\,q^H$ with $0<q<1$ and an empirical slope $\delta = -\log_{10}q \approx 0.8$. Under a relay-gain sufficient condition $C_{H+1}/C_H < R_{H+1}/R_H$ (with $C_H$ the formation cost and $R_H$ the in-era relay capacity), this geometric contraction follows directly as $\Delta_{H+1}/\Delta_H = (C_{H+1}/R_{H+1})/(C_H/R_H) = \eta/\gamma = q<1$. We treat this as an open conjecture in the present manuscript; the empirical model-selection test against constant-interval, power-law, finite-time singularity, and logistic-saturation alternatives, together with a record-density null, is the subject of Paper~11. The conjecture is included here only for forward reference, and is not used as an assumption in the present cross-sectional analysis.

\section{Materials and Methods}

\paragraph{Assignment order.}
For every primary-score row, relay depth \(H\) or mixture weights
\(\{\pi_k\}\) are assigned from structural evidence before
\(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}\) is used for evaluation.  Structural evidence covers
CPC composition, input--output layering, enterprise-size and occupational
structure, and network topology; slope-audit evidence (ML, BIC, nearest-rung
diagnostics) is used only to check internal coherence after the assignment
is fixed.

\paragraph{Continuous effective depth.}
Continuous \(\Heff\) is computed only as the inverse image of an integer-rung
mixture, \(\epsilon(\Heff)=\sum_k\pi_k\,\epsilon(H_k)\), and is not treated
as a primitive fitted depth.  It is a descriptive coordinate for predeclared
crossover rows and does not introduce an indicator-specific free parameter.

\paragraph{Measurement-frame conditioning.}
All cross-city exponent comparisons are conditioned on the city definition
(MSA, FUA, LUZ, national, or metropolitan), geographic scope, and time window
used to estimate \(\beta_{\mathrm{obs}}\).  Frames are not pooled unless the
measurement frame and mixture weights are explicitly harmonized with the
frame used for structural assignment.

\paragraph{Primary and secondary endpoints.}
The primary endpoint is paired prediction error on prespecified rows; CI
coverage, continuous-\(\Heff\) coverage, and McNemar-style paired changes
are reported as secondary descriptive diagnostics. Accordingly, CI coverage is a headline diagnostic, whereas paired loss and predeclared assignment replication are the primary statistical endpoints; a coverage drop to $21/22$ or below nonetheless serves as a binary falsifier for the predeclared hybrid ledger.  The
\(17/22\to 21/22\to 22/22\) waterfall is reported as a nested three-tier
ledger, not as three independent headline claims.

\paragraph{Outlier-gate rule.}
Rows declared as declining-sector outliers or boundary-definition stress
tests (CPC Section D coke/petroleum refining, Japan GDP under its most
restrictive definition) are retained in the SI, but they are not silently
mixed into the primary score unless the inclusion rule is stated before the
comparison.  All such inclusion rules are frozen at the SI level and
referenced rather than adjusted per row.

\paragraph{Numerical reference for the relay-depth exponent.}
For ease of reference, the predicted superlinear branch $\beta_+(H)$ values at integer relay depths are listed below:
$\beta_+(2)=1.311$, $\beta_+(3)=1.171$, $\beta_+(4)=1.114$, $\beta_+(5)=1.083$, $\beta_+(6)=1.065$, $\beta_+(7)=1.053$, $\beta_+(8)=1.044$, $\beta_+(H{\to}\infty)=1$. The first differences are $0.140, 0.057, 0.030, 0.018, 0.012, 0.009$, showing that the ladder predicts a \emph{monotonic convex relaxation toward $\beta{=}1$, not an arithmetic equal-spacing rule}. The mirror values for the sublinear branch are obtained by $\beta_-(H)=2-\beta_+(H)$. We therefore treat observed $\beta$ trajectories as effective $H$-mixture diagnostics rather than as evidence for any assumed equally-spaced universal sequence; this is the natural reading of the ladder formula $\varepsilon(H)=1/[H\ln(2H{+}1)]$ and is consistent with $\beta\!\to\!1$ at $H\!\to\!\infty$ being a continuous limit point of the integer ladder (no discrete jump required).

\section*{Significance Statement}

Urban scaling is usually described by fitting a separate slope to each indicator. Here a zero-fitted-exponent relay-depth ladder predicts exponents across the canonical 22-indicator panel via a three-tier decomposition: $12/22$ direct strict-integer matches (Tier A scoring rows), $5/22$ indirect single-$H$ closures (proxy / residual / reference rows), and $5/22$ continuous-$H_{\rm eff}$ Tier B rows (mixture closures: Gasoline sales / stations, AIDS, Inventors, Patents-legacy). Direct-strict 12-row MAE $= 0.008$, Tier-A-full 16-row MAE $= 0.017$, all-22 disclosed MAE $= 0.015$. Random-$H$ ladder selection achieves the 17-row Tier-A-full count with probability $<10^{-7}$ across three operational definitions (SI~\textsf{S-poisson-op-def}). The same framework places GDP in a BEA-consistent $H=4$--$5$ corridor rather than a shallow service class, and explains near-linear indicators by finite-depth cross-branch balance rather than an unrealistic $H\to\infty$ limit. Numerical conventions (analytical $\beta_\pm(H)$, $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ axiomatic-minimality framing, Random-$H$ op-def, MAE/RMSE three-tier reporting, three-tier headline disclosure) are specified in SI~\textsf{S-implementation-notes}. Urban exponents thus become testable structural classifications, not post hoc regressions.

\section*{Data and Code Availability}

All primary scaling exponents are from previously published
sources~\cite{Bettencourt2007,Bettencourt2013}.
Patent data were obtained from the USPTO PatentsView bulk data tables
(\href{https://s3.amazonaws.com/data.patentsview.org/download/}{s3.amazonaws.com/\allowbreak data.patentsview.org/\allowbreak download/}).
GDP sector shares were derived from BEA GDP-by-Industry and related
value-added tables.
MSA population data were obtained from the U.S. Census Bureau.

\section*{SI Appendix S-PanelOrigins. Era-of-Crystallisation audit of the Bettencourt 22-panel}\label{sec:S-PanelOrigins}

The Bettencourt 22-panel is treated in this paper as a single-epoch cross-sectional exponent benchmark. This appendix does not add a cross-time \(\beta\) test. It records only a carrier-era audit: the historical period in which each observable's measurement carrier, institutional substrate, or urban accounting form acquired its modern form. For late-observed proxies, such as AIDS, the carrier era-of-crystallisation (EOC) is the public-health surveillance and statistical-reporting system, not the first year of the disease-specific episode.

\textbf{Carrier-EOC classification (preliminary).} On carrier coding, most or all of the panel belongs to the industrial--electrical--petroleum--electronic substrate ramp of 1751--1971. Post-1971 disease-specific, software-specific, or measurement-slice realisations are treated as adaptations of earlier carriers unless explicitly flagged. This audit is descriptive metadata and is not part of the \(22/22\) CI-coverage score.

\textbf{Reading guide.} Rows are sorted by $\beta_{\rm obs}$ midpoint (ascending) and partitioned into two coverage tiers: \textbf{Tier A --- integer-rung tier (17/22)}, and \textbf{Tier B --- the additional five rows that complete the $22/22$ closure under the central $H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster framework, sub-decomposed as $+2$ same-branch sublinear composition (Gasoline sales / Gasoline stations), $+2$ continuous correction-space $\Heff$ sensitivity (Disease/AIDS, Inventors), and $+1$ hybrid/legacy closure (Patents Bettencourt~2007 retention)}; in all five Tier B rows, $H_{\rm eff}$ is reported only as a sensitivity coordinate and not as a fitted explanatory parameter. This appendix is an era-of-crystallisation audit rather than the authoritative numerical scoring table; the numerical ledger remains the one stated in the Results: $17/22$ strict integer, $+2$ same-branch sublinear composition, $+2$ continuous correction-space $\Heff$ sensitivity, and $+1$ final hybrid/legacy closure, giving $22/22$. The $\beta$ columns below are retained only as identifiers copied from the panel audit; they must not be read as a second independent scoring table.

\textit{The relay-depth framework reaches $\beta\!\approx\!1$ via three non-$H\!\to\!\infty$ paths} (none requires the formal $H\!\to\!\infty$ jump):
(i) \textbf{Path~1 — cross-branch cancellation at single integer $H$}: a mixture of $+$ and $-$ branches with generation-coverage asymmetry $\sigma_{gc}{=}\pi_{+}{-}\pi_{-}{=}0$ produces $\beff{=}1{+}\sigma_{gc}\,\epsH{H}{=}1$ (linear attractor; main \S\ref{subsec:cross_branch_balance}). Used by the 5 ``balanced'' near-linear indicators in Tier A.
(ii) \textbf{Path~2 — continuous $\Heff$ + Jensen convexity}: single-branch convex averaging $\epsH{\Heff}{=}\sum_k\pi_k\,\epsH{H_k}$ over a smooth $H_k$ distribution (main \S\ref{subsec:H_selforg_conjecture} class). Used by the four non-Patents continuous-$\Heff$ sensitivity rows.
(iii) \textbf{Path~2 (extended) — central $K{=}2$, $H{=}\{2,3\}$ discrete integer cluster mixture}: applies uniformly to all 5 mixture-row indicators (Gasoline sales, Gasoline stations, AIDS deaths, Inventors, Patents (US)), with the cluster structure supplying the assignment per indicator. The Patents (US) anchor is included in this central protocol; no separate $H{=}\{1,2\}$ exception path is required, since the Heff value $\approx 2.10$ for Patents is the equivalence point of the $H{=}\{2,3\}$ mixture.
The integer ladder is therefore continuously connected to $\beta{=}1$ at finite $H$ via three independent mechanisms; no discrete jump to $H\!\to\!\infty$ is required.

\noindent{\footnotesize $^{\dagger}$ \textbf{Patent strict audit panel}: row 17 reports the reproducible USPTO--CBSA cross-section (2010 patents vs 2010 census population, $n=378$ strict-audit slice common with the GDP indicator panel; the all-MSA stability slice $n=386$ yields $\hat\beta=1.294$, reported in the main text), with $\hat\beta=1.298$ and OLS-standard 95\% CI $[1.198, 1.398]$, which contains the ladder prediction $\beta_+(2)=1.311$. The seminal Bettencourt et al.~(2007) PNAS interval $[1.25, 1.29]$ (row 22), part of the foundational urban-scaling literature on which the present analytic framework builds~\cite{Bettencourt2007,Bettencourt2013}, is here re-examined for the specific purpose of integer-ladder testing. Because the original interval was not constructed for the one-year cross-sectional ladder audit performed here, we treat it as a legacy reference interval rather than as a strict cross-sectional exclusion interval for the present test. Its narrow half-width $0.02$ likely reflects a different (e.g., pooled MSA-year, covariance-adjusted, or effective-$n$-enlarged) estimation methodology distinct from the one-year MSA cross-sectional OLS framework adopted here. $^{\ddagger}$ \textbf{Bettencourt 2007 legacy retention (row 22)}: included for cross-paper continuity with the published 22-panel literature; the $H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster mixture $\beta_{\rm pred}=1.289$ lies inside the published interval, consistent with the hybrid protocol. $^{\dagger\dagger}$ \textbf{GDP row 12 (US, OECD) reference only}: the displayed $\beta_{\rm obs}{=}1.13\sim 1.26$ aggregates several cross-country definitions and is reported here as an EOC midpoint reference, not as a strict-integer scoring entry; the matched US-MSA panel value is row 13 ($\beta_{\rm obs}{=}1.099$ MSA-mean), which sits within the $\{3,4,5\}$ mixture corridor at $\Heff{\approx}4.42$ and is the value scored in the main panel ledger.\par}

\paragraph{Status column legend and provenance audit.}
The new \textbf{Status} column in the table above partitions the 22 panel rows by direct-observation provenance and is provided as an audit transparency tool rather than as a new scoring layer. The values are: \textit{strict} ($n=12$, direct cross-sectional $\beta_{\rm obs}$ observation under the panel-canonical pipeline), \textit{proxy} ($n=3$, substituted from an adjacent canonical row when the original quantity is not separately measured: Households~$\leftarrow$~Housing units, Crime indices~$\leftarrow$~AIDS, Ph.D.~holders~$\leftarrow$~Supercreative), \textit{residual} ($n=1$, derived analytically as the linear-attractor closure when no direct $\beta_{\rm obs}$ is reported in the panel: Establishments), \textit{reference} ($n=1$, period-aggregated row included for audit cross-walk and not for primary scoring: GDP US-OECD row 12, see footnote $^{\dagger\dagger}$ above), \textit{mixture} ($n=4$, $H{=}\{2,3\}$ explicit two-component closure rows), and \textit{legacy} ($n=1$, included for cross-paper continuity with the published 22-panel literature: Patents Bettencourt 2007 row 22). The strict count $17/22$ headline reported in the main text therefore decomposes into $12$ direct strict rows plus $5$ audit-qualified single-$H$ closures (1 residual + 3 proxy + 1 reference), with the remaining $4$ explicit $H{=}\{2,3\}$ mixtures and $1$ legacy comparator row completing the panel. The Status column does not alter any $\beta_{\rm pred}$ value, mixture weight, or central-protocol assignment; $H$ values for proxy and residual rows are inherited from their canonical source under the panel-canonical pipeline, and mixture-row $H_{\rm eff}$ values remain analytically derived from the discrete integer cluster $H{=}\{2,3\}$ as documented in the main body (Stage~4). The audit is descriptive metadata and is not used as an additional fitting layer.

\paragraph{Closure sensitivity for Patents.} The gap between the Bettencourt point estimate $\beta_{\rm obs}=1.270$ and the strict $H=2$ ladder prediction $\beta_{\rm pred}=1.311$ is $\Delta\beta=0.041$. Three measurement-side mechanisms can each produce a flattening of this magnitude in a single-year MSA cross-section: (i) MSA boundary instability under PMSA/CBSA vintage changes — for a multiplicative splitting law $k(N)\propto N^a$ across superlinear quantities, $\beta_{\rm obs}\simeq\beta_H-(\beta_H-1)\,a$, so $a\simeq 0.13$ reproduces $\Delta\beta=0.041$; (ii) a near-linear external component of share $s\simeq 13\%$ (corporate filing aggregation, PCT cross-border filing, assignee-inventor address mismatch), via $\beta_{\rm obs}\simeq(1-s)\beta_H+s\gamma$ with $\gamma\simeq 1$; (iii) a closure-retention gradient $r_i\propto N_i^{-\eta}$ with $\eta\simeq 0.041$, equivalent to large metros leaking $\sim 17\%$ of local patent production to suburbs/satellites under residence-vs-workplace assignment. The Cowork reproducible USPTO--CBSA audit shows the strict CI containment is preserved under modern panel construction, so the closure sensitivity is reported as theoretical robustness rather than as a fitted correction.

\paragraph{Ladder-constrained mixture diagnostic.} A ladder-integer constrained\linebreak mixture-of-regressions over the USPTO--CBSA 2010 panel (Gaussian mixture with fixed\linebreak slopes $\beta_+(H)\in\{1.910,1.311,1.171\}$ for $H\in\{1,2,3\}$, fitting only the mixture weights $\pi_k$, intercepts $c_k$ and within-cluster scales $\sigma_k$) selects the $H=2$ branch: at $K=3$ the BIC-preferred specification has $(\hat\pi_1,\hat\pi_2,\hat\pi_3)\simeq(0,0.99,0)$ with $\beta_{\rm mix}=1.312\approx\beta_+(2)$. The $K=2$ specification with $H\!\in\!\{2,3\}$ is BIC-rejected ($\Delta{\rm BIC}=-26.93$ in favour of $K=3$), but the collapsed-simplex $K=3$ solution is physically equivalent to a single-component $H=2$ substrate rather than evidence for three coexisting patent phases. We therefore interpret the diagnostic as confirming the strict $H=2$ assignment for the Patents observable.

\paragraph{Three-window counts.} Of the 22 indicators above, $\hat{n}_{[1751,1971]} = 22$ fall predominantly in the silent-Kramers corridor; $\hat{n}_{[1472,1751]} = 0$ in the H=4 stable interval (book-printing indicators are not in this panel); $\hat{n}_{[\text{post}1971]} = 0$ in the modern compute era. We note that some indicators (e.g., gasoline-sales, R\&D, high-tech employment) are 20th-century late-modernity events with EOC near the corridor terminus 1971, while others (patents, banking) had earlier crystallisations in the 19th century. A bootstrap (n=10000) on EOC midpoints with $\pm 30$~yr uncertainty per indicator yields the 95\% CI for the 1751--1971 window count of $[18, 22]$.

\paragraph{Closure protocol independence.} The closure protocol used here estimates $\beta$ from cross-sectional log-log scaling at a single observation epoch (typically 1990--2010); the protocol is therefore independent of the indicators' crystallisation eras. We document the EOC audit here only to align the present cross-sectional anchor with the Paper 3 alternate wholesale-adoption interpretation, in which the 1751--1971 silent-Kramers corridor is the era during which the 22-panel indicators acquired their modern observational form. The closure result (22/22 CI overlap with the integer-cluster-mixture predictions) is unchanged irrespective of which Paper 3 mapping (baseline or alternate wholesale-adoption interpretation) is adopted.

\paragraph{Falsifier.} If the EOC audit shows that significantly fewer than 18 indicators fall in the 1751--1971 corridor (e.g., $\hat{n}_{[1751,1971]} < 12$ at 95\% CI), the alternate silent-Kramers reading would lose empirical alignment and the baseline 1472--1971 H=4 stable mapping would be re-prioritised. Pre-registered: the EOC midpoint dataset and bootstrap CI computation script will be published alongside this deposit.

\multirow[c]{5}{*}{\rotatebox[origin=c]{90}{\shortstack[c]{\textbf{Path 2 extended:}\\[3pt]\textbf{hybrid (+5)}}}}
 & gasoline sales & physical infra. (demand-flow caveat) & area-bounded, road/fueling delivery & \(-\), \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) mix & 0.790 & \makecell[ct]{0.79 \\ {[0.73, 0.80]}} & Qualified match. Flow on station + road vehicle-km substrate. \\
 & gasoline stations & physical infra. & area/vol.-bounded & \(-\), \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) mix & 0.790 & \makecell[ct]{0.77 \\ {[0.74, 0.81]}} & Match. Parcel-based facilities; bounded land/storage. \\
 & AIDS cases & socio-econ coord. & unbounded dens. & \(+\), \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) mix & 1.230 & \makecell[ct]{1.23 \\ {[1.18, 1.29]}} & Match. Contact/reporting network densification. \\
 & new AIDS & socio-econ coord. & unbounded dens. & \(+\), \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) mix & 1.230 & \makecell[ct]{1.23 \\ {[1.18, 1.29]}} & Match. Event flow on same contact-network substrate as stock. \\
 & inventors & socio-econ coord. & unbounded dens. & \(+\), \(H{=}\{2,3\}\) mix & 1.250 & \makecell[ct]{1.25 \\ {[1.22, 1.27]}} & Match. Labor/knowledge-network role, not area-bounded. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}

\smallskip
\noindent{\footnotesize \textit{Match criterion}: ``Match'' indicates that (i) the structurally derived branch sign (\(\sigma\in\{+,-\}\)) agrees with the sign of \(\beta_{\rm obs}-1\), and (ii) the analytical \(\beta_{\rm pred}\) falls inside the reported 95\,\% confidence interval of \(\beta_{\rm obs}\). ``Qualified'' indicates a hybrid / definition-sensitive row whose substrate constraint is mixed (electricity, housing); these rows are not used as clean evidence in the headline closure count.}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.0}
\end{table}

The 22-row assignment is retrospective for the present panel (= no public freeze pre-existed before \(\beta_{\rm obs}\) was observed); however, the network-type and substrate-constraint columns can be reproduced from publicly available indicator definitions and standard urban-system descriptions, so the assignment is structurally pre-\(\beta\) in form even though the registry freeze itself awaits the companion data release (Zenodo v1.3+). All 20 of 22 rows show structural agreement; the two ``hybrid / expert review'' rows (electricity, housing) are flagged and not used as clean evidence in the \(22/22\) coverage claim.

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-CrossTimeBeta. Pre-1971 \(H\)-era ladder and withdrawal of the previously proposed numerical \(\beta\)-bridge}\label{sec:S-CrossTimeBeta}

The present paper measures the relay-depth \(H\) within the Paper~3 \(\Omega\)-domain, hence its scope is bounded by the natural span of \(\Omega\equiv\int N^{2}\,dt\) before the post-1971 substrate handoff (see the Scope-boundary paragraph in the Discussion above). This appendix retains the pre-1971 portion of the \(H\)-era ladder as the temperature-measurement reference table for the main body. The retained rungs run from the hunter--gatherer \(H{=}1\) era through the H${=}$4$\to$5 silent-Kramers corridor that ends at the 1971 TFR-peak lock. The post-1971 substrate-relay era (treated in Paper~5) is removed from this appendix; readers requiring the post-1971 cascade evidence should consult Paper~5 Supplementary Information.

The pre-registered protocol applied here is: log\(_{10}\) transformation + OLS--Huber regression + leave-one-out (LOO) sensitivity + BCa bootstrap 95\% CI + \(\Delta\)BIC\(\geq\)10 for model selection + Jensen convexity for mixture detection + \(N\geq30\) per epoch + TOST equivalence test against the analytical \(\beta_{\pm}(H)\) predictions, with post-hoc fitting prohibited.

\paragraph{Note on $H{=}1$.} The hunter--gatherer band substrate ($H{=}1$, pre-Neolithic, $\sim$10\,kya and earlier; band size 12--150) is excluded from the cross-time $\beta$ campaign because (i) ethnographic and archaeological band-size estimates carry $>50\%$ uncertainty per population proxy, swamping any $\beta\!-\!1$ signal at the achievable $N$; and (ii) the present paper's central protocol uses the integer pair $H{=}\{2,3\}$ cluster mixture and does not invoke an $H{=}1$ weight in modern indicators. The ladder predicts $\beta_+(H{=}1)=1+1/(1\cdot\ln 3)\approx 1.910$ at $H{=}1$, which is therefore covered analytically without requiring a dedicated cross-time data campaign.

\paragraph{Two distinct $\beta$ measurement types and their disambiguation.}
The pre-1971 cross-time ladder retained in this appendix predicts era-specific values of a \emph{single-population} scaling exponent $\beta_+(H)$: in a given era, the slope from a single cross-sectional log--log regression of an output observable $Y$ (patents, GDP, energy, etc.) against total substrate population $N$, evaluated under a fixed era-typical relay depth $H$. The central claim of the present paper, by contrast, is a \emph{cluster-mixture central H value} measured at a single modern epoch: the integer-mixture protocol over functional cluster components of the Bettencourt 22-indicator panel, which under $d{=}3$ urban embedding identifies the active cluster pair as H$=\{2,3\}$ and delivers a 22/22 hybrid closure (Stage~4 of the Results). The two measurement types are formally distinct: the predicted-$\beta_+$ column in the H$_{\rm era}$ table below is a forecast of the single-population trajectory, whereas the main-text Stage~1--4 results are anchored in the cluster-mixture central H. An empirical anti-falsification of one therefore does not mechanically falsify the other, and the 22/22 hybrid closure of the Bettencourt panel is independent of the previously proposed numerical bridge that connected them in earlier drafts.

\paragraph{Era-window tunability (Paper~5 sync).} The era windows below are pre-registered targets aligned with Paper~5's substrate-equivalence dataset and Paper~3's silent-Kramers corridor mapping (alternate wholesale-adoption interpretation; see Paper~3 SI Appendix S-StrictFigureReading). They may be refined by $\pm$30--50 yr if Paper~5's cross-substrate measurements (DNA / brain / silicon / river / stellar) sharpen the boundary between successive integer $H$ rungs; any such adjustment will be re-registered in an errata note for the present paper before the corresponding $\beta$ measurement is released. Recent multi-source corroboration (Bai--Perron + PELT + BottomUp three-method analysis) detected internal sub-corridor candidates near 1820 (silent-era onset; Maddison $p=0.003$), 1900 (1880--1913; 3/5 modern series strict agreement among energy, urbanisation, literacy), and 1950 (1945--1965; 2/5 strict and 4/5 directional agreement) within the 1751--1971 (H${=}$4$\to$5) corridor; an AD 100--235 transition corridor was also detected around the H${=}$2 stable end (AD 151 as labelled midpoint, with EDCS apex at AD 100--150 and CHRE crisis inflection at AD 200--235). These sub-structure candidates remain within the $\pm$30--50 yr re-registration window and will be formalised after Paper~5 cross-substrate verification. The $H$ rung values themselves are integer-fixed by the relay-depth ladder and are \emph{not} tunable.

\clearpage  % V167 FIX 84: force longtable to start on a fresh page (V166 author feedback: table が 2 ページに跨る場合に table 前で改ページ必要)
% V206 FIX 210+217

1 & $-70$k$\sim$$-12$k & Hunter-gatherer bands (ethnographic + archaeological proxies) & 1.910 (analytical) & N$\geq$20 bands (footnote-only; band-size noise) \\
1$\to$2 & $-12$k$\sim$$-5$k & Neolithic: Younger-Dryas + early agriculture; site sizes (Natufian $\Phi_S$ sub-critical) & corridor (steep $\epsilon$ drop) & N$\geq$20 archaeological units; 14C SPD bins \\
2 & $-5$k$\sim$151 & Roman/Han/Mauryan-Gupta (Hanson, ORBIS, Duncan-Jones) & 1.311 & N$\geq$30 cities/provinces \\

4 & 1472$\sim$1751 & Printing+commerce (USTC/ESTC, Sound Toll, Amsterdam, BoE) & 1.114 & N$\geq$30 European cities \\
4$\to$5 & 1751$\sim$1971 & Industrial/electrical/petroleum (USPTO, EIA, BP, OWID; silent Kramers) & 1.05 (silent-corridor empirical estimate; not a ladder integer)$^{\ast}$ & N$\geq$30 states/countries \\
\end{longtable}
}

\noindent{\footnotesize $^{\ast}$ \textbf{$1.05$ silent-corridor row entry}: the value $\beta\!\approx\!1.05$ for the 1751--1971 corridor is an empirical estimate over the 220\,yr silent-Kramers transition window, distinct from the integer the ladder rungs $\beta_{+}(4)=1.114$ and $\beta_{+}(5)=1.083$ that bracket the corridor. The integer rungs are the ladder predictions; $1.05$ is the within-corridor empirical average expected under the alternate wholesale-adoption interpretation.\par}

\paragraph{Note on corridor boundary years.} The corridor onsets and ends 151\,/\,734\,/\,1221\,/\,1472 in the table above are inherited from the companion Paper~3~\cite{Kato2026c} exogenous-ceiling simulations. There the Dark-Age (151\,$\sim$\,734\,CE) and Black-Death (1221\,$\sim$\,1472\,CE) corridor onsets are triggered when the dimensionless demographic-pressure ratio $N/V_F\geq 1.4$ produces a col-event (population-floor break) on the historical $H_{\rm era}\!\to\!N$ log-log trajectory; the boundary years are the corresponding simulation-crossing intersections, not free fitted parameters. More specifically, they are the inter-phase crossings of a four-phase Paper~3 trajectory (phase~1: $-70$k\,--\,$-30$k pre-needle Toba recovery at $H{=}1$ fluctuation level; phase~2: $-30$k\,--\,$-12$k post-needle $\Omega_{\rm competitive\_coop}\!+\!\Omega_{\rm territory\_tool}$ stable interval with $C_2$ tool-inheritance maturity; phase~3: $-12$k\,--\,$-5$k $H{=}1\!\to\!2$ Younger-Dryas Kramers nucleation; phase~4: $-5$k\,--\,151\,CE Verhulst--VF dual-propulsion main integration window; see Paper~3 SI Appendix S-Phase\linebreak Boundaries). The AD~151 boundary in particular is the labelled midpoint of an AD~100\,$\sim$\,235 transition corridor bounded by the EDCS apex (Roman institutional zenith at AD~100--150) and the CHRE crisis inflection (Roman-collapse onset at AD~200--235), with the Hanson direct rate ratio of $0.023$ (97.7\,\% collapse) anchoring the corridor's terminal end. The simulation crossings establish each $H_{\rm era}$ boundary structurally; the Bettencourt 22-panel cross-sectional benchmark (this paper's main empirical content) operates entirely within the silent-Kramers corridor culminating at 1971, so the boundaries above orient the era classification used here but are not themselves measured by it. See Paper~3 for the full simulation protocol, $\Omega$-naming canonical, and corridor characterisations.

\paragraph{Empirical audit status of the predicted-\(\beta_+\) ladder for the H${=}$4$\to$5 closing entry.} The 1971 boundary at the end of the pre-1971 ladder is itself under empirical audit. A direct USPTO-based per-decade \(\beta\) trajectory covering 1900--2025 (HistPat 1900--1975 + USPTO PatentsView 1976--2025) is reported in Paper~5 Supplementary Information. Three substantive findings are carried forward to the present paper: (a) the H${=}$4$\to$5 boundary year at 1971\(\pm\)5 is partially vindicated (Bai--Perron single-changepoint scan places the dominant break at 1965, in window); (b) the boundary level is anti-falsified (the empirical single-population \(\beta\) also trends upward across the 1971-vicinity break, matching the direction of the predicted small upward shift \(\beta\!\approx\!1.05\!\to\!\)H${=}$5 \(\beta\!=\!1.083\) implied by the 4$\to$5 row of the table; however, the empirical trajectory does not lock at the H${=}$5 ladder rung \(1.083\) but overshoots to \(\beta\!\approx\!1.32\) by 2021--25, exceeding the predicted level by a wide margin); (c) the boundary-level prediction is anti-falsified at three anchors (1900--04 \(\beta=0.66 \ll 1.20\); 1940--60 \(\beta=0.95 \ll 1.114\); 2021--25 \(\beta=1.32 \gg 1.065\)). The empirical trajectory is therefore consistent with the timing structure of the H$_{\rm era}$ ladder (a real structural break does occur near 1971), but not with the specific levels: the predicted ladder transition from H${=}$4 ($\beta_+(4)=1.114$) to H${=}$5 ($\beta_+(5)=1.083$) corresponds to a small downward step on the integer ladder, while within the silent corridor the predicted small upward shift from $\beta\!\approx\!1.05$ to $1.083$ at the H${=}$5 lock is itself overshot in the empirical trajectory by a wide margin (reaching $\beta\!\approx\!1.32$ by 2021--25). Paper~5 SI develops a measurement-type-aware reconciliation under which the single-population \(\beta\) trajectory and the present cluster-mixture H ladder are not the same observable.

\paragraph{Pre-registered $\beta$-shift signatures across rung transitions.} Three pre-registered shift detection windows accompany the pre-1971 rung-specific reconstructions: (i) $-100$ to $200$~CE Roman vs 800--1200 Carolingian/Tang--Song shift ($\beta_+$ from $\sim 1.311$ to $\sim 1.171$, signature of H${=}$2$\to$3); (ii) 1450--1517 vs 1517--1789 vs 1789--1850 Reformation $\Phi_N$-gateway shift (testing whether the H${=}$4 narrative-completion band 1517--1789 shows a discrete $\beta$ jump); (iii) 1965--1975 TFR-peak shift (whether the silent-Kramers $\beta\approx 1.05$ converges to the H${=}$5 lock value $\beta=1.083$ at 1971). Each window follows pre-registered analysis protocols (trio of window-shift detection methods: pre/post sub-period bootstrap CI for shift magnitude and significance, bias-corrected accelerated intervals with $B=10{,}000$ resamples per window) detailed in the SI methodology section. \emph{Empirical outcome for window~(iii):} the USPTO + HistPat 1900--2025 trajectory shows a structural break inside the 1965--1975 window (Bai--Perron single at 1965; Bai--Perron triple at 1926/1965/2000; PELT places nearby breaks at 1961 and 1964 at low penalties), the shift direction is \emph{upward} and is in agreement with the predicted small upward shift $\beta\!\approx\!1.05\!\to\!1.083$ in direction, but the empirical step magnitude vastly exceeds the predicted level (overshooting to $\beta\!\approx\!1.32$ by 2021--25); the boundary year is partially vindicated, the boundary level is not. Outcomes for windows~(i) and~(ii) are not reported here pending the Paper~3 SI cross-time companion.

\paragraph{Notation crosswalk for the boundary spine.}
Throughout the present paper the 1971 transition is labelled consistently as \(H=4\to5\) under the cluster-mixture central-\(H\) framework, in agreement with the Paper~3 alternative wholesale-adoption interpretation of 1751--1971 as a silent \(H=4\to5\) Kramers corridor culminating at the 1971 TFR-peak lock. The 1820 boundary is labelled as the industrial-onset corridor entry within the same \(H=4\to5\) silent-Kramers reading. The AD~151 boundary is labelled at the Roman-peak end of the antiquity (\(H=2\)) phase. No stray \(H=3\to4\) labelling is used for any post-1971 phenomenon.

\paragraph{Withdrawal of the previously proposed numerical \(\beta\)-bridge.}
The previously proposed numerical bridge from \(H\)-era rungs to a single-population \(\beta\) trajectory is withdrawn. The USPTO inventor-fractional audit does not support that bridge and therefore cannot be used as a validation of the present paper. The audit concerns a Bettencourt-style log--log slope for a specified output, geography, and population denominator; it is not a direct measurement of the latent cluster-mixture \(H\) state. The present paper retains only the AD~151 / 1820 / 1971 cluster-mixture boundary spine and the pre-1971 H${=}$1$\to$4$\to$5 rung table above. The bridge is not replaced by a post-hoc inversion, and no revised single-population \(\beta\) ladder is released here; any such ladder, if it is ever developed, is the responsibility of Paper~5 SI and Paper~3 SI.

\paragraph{The $\Omega$-era catalogue and its cross-paper layering.}
The ten-phase $\Omega$-era catalogue used in this paper---$\Omega_{\rm competitive\_coop}$, $\Omega_{\rm territory\_tool}$, $\Omega_{\rm food\_pre\_irrig}$, $\Omega_{\rm food\_post\_irrig}$, $\Omega_{\rm dark\_age}$,\linebreak $\Omega_{\rm empire\_writing}$, $\Omega_{\rm black\_death}$, $\Omega_{\rm capital\_printing}$, $\Omega_{\rm industry\_science}$, $\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}$---is the ten-phase classification used here, also adopted by the substrate-relay cascade discussion of Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e}. This paper uses the ten-phase form because the 1971 boundary employed here lies precisely at the $\Omega_{\rm industry\_science}\!\to\!\Omega_{\rm longlife\_computing}$ transition.

\paragraph{Beyond 1971: forward reference.}
Post-1971 substrate-relay evidence (including digital-economy anchors and the USPTO inventor-fractional $\beta$ audit) is developed in Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e} and its Supplementary Information; none of that post-1971 evidence is used in the present paper to support the pre-1971 chronology, in keeping with the scope rule already stated above.

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-implementation-notes. Numerical convention and computation specifications}\label{sec:S-KNOWN-ISSUES-integrated}

\sloppy
This appendix specifies the numerical conventions and computational definitions adopted in the present analysis. The five notes below state the convention or definition in use, together with the corresponding reproducibility script in \texttt{scripts/}.

\textbf{Note~1 --- Simulation script convention.} The simulation script \texttt{scripts/sim\_paper4\_22\_22\_full\_impl\_v4.py} computes all rung values analytically from $\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$ and follows the SI Primary Panel Table $H$-assignment verbatim (no greedy search). The analytical rung values are $\beta_+(1)=1.910$, $\beta_+(2)=1.311$, $\beta_+(3)=1.171$, $\beta_-(2)=0.689$, $\beta_-(3)=0.829$.

\textbf{Note~2 --- $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ reporting framework.} The relay-depth ladder is selected on \emph{axiomatic minimality} (A1--A4 $\Rightarrow$ $z(H)=2H+1$) rather than on empirical AIC uniqueness. Several near-equivalent state-count forms ($\epsilon\!=\!1/H^{2}$, $1/[H\ln(3H+1)]$, $1/[H\ln(H+1)]$) attain CI / MAE / AIC values comparable to the relay-depth ladder on the 22-indicator panel under per-row best-$H$ optimisation; this empirical cluster of near-equivalents is documented in SI~\textsf{S-epsilon-alternative-rejection}. The alternative-formula block of the simulation script is shipped alongside.

\textbf{Note~3 --- Random-$H$ null operational definition.} Under the natural operational definition $H\!\sim\!\mathrm{Uniform}\{2,\dots,8\}$ with branch matched to indicator regime, the Poisson-binomial probability of attaining the 17-row Tier-A-full count is $P\!<\!10^{-7}$ across the three op-defs explored (see SI~\textsf{S-poisson-op-def}); the substantive non-randomness ($z\!>\!5$) is preserved. The reproducible DP computation is \texttt{scripts/poisson\_binomial\_random\_H.py}.

\textbf{Note~4 --- MAE / RMSE three-tier reporting.} The canonical script \texttt{scripts/paper4\_mae\_rmse\_canonical.py} reports three slices separately, reflecting the three-tier scoring framework adopted in this paper: (a)~direct-strict 12-row Tier A: $\mathrm{MAE}\!=\!0.008$, $\mathrm{RMSE}\!=\!0.010$; (b)~Tier A full 16 scored rows (= direct + indirect, Establishments residual skipped): $\mathrm{MAE}\!=\!0.017$, $\mathrm{RMSE}\!=\!0.030$; (c)~all-22 with the Tier-B \emph{ex post} mixing-coordinate diagnostic disclosed: $\mathrm{MAE}\!=\!0.015$, $\mathrm{RMSE}\!=\!0.027$. The paper headline uses slice (a) direct-strict 12-row MAE $0.008$ as the primary number alongside the Tier-A-full and all-22 disclosed values for slice transparency.

\textbf{Note~5 --- Three-tier headline disclosure.} The 22-indicator panel scoring is decomposed as $12/22$ direct strict-integer matches (Tier A scoring rows) plus $5/22$ indirect single-$H$ closures (proxy / residual / reference rows) plus $5/22$ Tier-B continuous-$H_{\rm eff}$ closures (an \emph{ex post} mixing-coordinate diagnostic on the pre-specified $H\!=\!\{2,3\}$ ladder, pending independent network-feature verification; see SI~\textsf{S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate} \S2'' for the companion universal $\beta$ predictor tool). Abstract, Significance Statement, Fig.\,1 box, and SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins} state this three-tier disclosure uniformly. The framework is falsified by a drop in the Tier-A direct-strict count to $11/22$ or below.

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-poisson-op-def. Operational definition of the random-$H$ null and Poisson-binomial DP}\label{sec:S-poisson-op-def}

\sloppy
We make explicit the operational definition of the ``random $H$ assignment'' null used in the main-text claim that the Tier-A direct-strict count is not reproducible by chance. Three op-defs are considered.

\textbf{(A) Headline:} $H_i\sim\mathrm{Uniform}\{2,\dots,8\}$ independently for each indicator $i$; the branch sign $\pm$ is matched to the empirical regime (super: $+$; sub: $-$; linear: structural balanced prediction $\beta\!=\!1$).

\textbf{(B) Random-branch:} $H_i\sim\mathrm{Uniform}\{2,\dots,8\}$ and branch $\sim\mathrm{Uniform}\{+,-\}$ independently, with no regime matching.

\textbf{(C) Extended-$H$:} $H_i\sim\mathrm{Uniform}\{1,\dots,8\}$ with branch matched to regime as in (A).

For each indicator $i$ and op-def, $p_i$ is the probability that the random pick lands within the published 95\,\% CI. The number of hits $X = \sum_i \mathbb{1}_{i\in\mathrm{CI}}$ is Poisson-binomial-distributed and $P(X\!\ge\!k)$ is evaluated by exact dynamic programming. The reproducible computation is \texttt{scripts/poisson\_binomial\_random\_H.py}.

Under all three op-defs the Poisson-binomial probability of attaining the Tier-A direct-strict count ($k\!=\!12$) is below $10^{-2}$ and the probability of attaining $k\!\ge\!17$ is below $10^{-7}$. We adopt op-def~(A) as the headline value. The earlier quotation $3.6\!\times\!10^{-15}$ is downgraded to this op-def-explicit threshold.

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-epsilon-alternative-rejection. Recomputed empirical comparison of state-count formulae (dual-panel transparency)}
\sloppy\label{sec:S-epsilon-alternative-rejection}

We recompute the empirical fit of six state-count formulae under two complementary panel scopes, both reaching the same qualitative conclusion: the ladder is near-equivalent to several state-count rivals on empirical loss, and is selected by axiomatic minimality rather than by empirical uniqueness.

\paragraph{Panel A --- reviewer naive replication (22-row best-$H$ blind search).}
A reviewer who runs an independent audit script over all 22 indicators with per-row best $H\!\in\!\{2,\dots,8\}$ and branch matched to regime, without applying the Path-1 cross-branch cancellation rule for near-linear rows, will obtain the numbers in Table~\ref{tab:alt_panelA}. This is the reference panel for external reproducibility. The corresponding reference script is \texttt{reviewer\_audit.py} / \texttt{alt\_state\_counts.py} (independent third-party audit) and the alternative-formula block (Panel A) of \texttt{scripts/sim\_paper4\_22\_22\_full\_impl\_v4.py} (paper-side reproduction).

\begin{table}[!h]
\caption{Panel A. Reviewer naive replication, 22-row best-$H$ blind search ($H\!\in\!\{2,\dots,8\}$, branch matched to regime, no Path-1 treatment). Numbers are reproducible from both the independent third-party audit script and the paper-side script. The simple AIC under $\sigma\!=\!\mathrm{RMSE}$ is reported as $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ relative to the empirical best (negative AIC favours smaller $\sigma$).}
\label{tab:alt_panelA}
\centering
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule
Formula & CI / 22 & MAE & RMSE & AIC \\
\midrule
Relay-depth $1/[H\ln(2H+1)]$               & 19/22 & 0.0255 & 0.0315 & $-89.76$ \\
$1/H^{2}$                           & $\mathbf{21/22}$ & 0.0250 & 0.0332 & $-87.46$ \\
$1/[H\ln(3H+1)]$                    & 19/22 & $\mathbf{0.0225}$ & $\mathbf{0.0294}$ & $\mathbf{-92.79}$ \\
$1/[H\ln(H+1)]$                     & 19/22 & 0.0249 & 0.0343 & $-86.02$ \\

$1/[(2H+1)\ln(2H+1)]$               & 15/22 & 0.0500 & 0.0770 & $-50.38$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\paragraph{Panel B --- paper framework with Path-1 cross-branch cancellation and Tier-A scoring rule.}
Under the paper's actual framework (SI~\textsf{S-path1-microfoundation}), the five near-linear indicators (Housing units, Households, Household water, Employment, Establishments) are not freely fitted with an integer rung but are structurally locked to $\beta\!=\!1$ via cross-branch cancellation $\sigma_{gc}\!=\!0$. The Tier-A scoring panel therefore consists of 17 rows (12 direct strict + 5 audit-qualified proxy / residual / reference rows), with the 5 balanced rows reported separately as a structural Path-1 closure and the 5 Tier-B rows as a continuous-$H_{\rm eff}$ closure. The alternative-formula recomputation on this restricted scoring panel yields the numbers in Table~\ref{tab:alt_panelB}. The reproducible computation is the alternative-formula block (Panel B) of \texttt{scripts/sim\_paper4\_22\_22\_full\_impl\_v4.py}.

\label{tab:alt_panelB}

\begin{tabular}{lccc}
