\end{table}

\paragraph{Joint reading and framework note.} The two panels differ in their treatment of the five near-linear indicators: Panel~A searches over $H\!\in\!\{2,\dots,8\}$ for those rows as well (typically picking $H\!=\!8$, $\beta\!=\!1.044$, which misses the tight CIs of Housing and Employment), while Panel~B treats them as Path-1 balanced rows with $\beta\!=\!1$ exact. The numerical accounting differs accordingly. Both panels agree on the central qualitative finding: the relay-depth ladder is in a cluster of empirically near-equivalent state-count formulae rather than being a unique empirical best, and the previous claim that it attains the lowest $\Delta\mathrm{AIC}$ relative to all alternatives is not reproduced under either panel scope. We therefore select the relay-depth ladder on axiomatic minimality alone (SI~\textsf{S-axiom-minimality}). The dual-panel reporting is offered so that a reviewer reproducing the audit obtains numbers consistent with both an independent third-party script (Panel A) and the paper's stated framework (Panel B).

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-axiom-minimality. Axiom system A1-A4 derivation of $z(H)=2H+1$ and alternative-formula axiom violations}
\sloppy\label{sec:S-axiom-minimality}

\paragraph{Part 1. Formal axiom statement.}
Let \(H\in\mathbb N=\{1,2,\ldots\}\) denote integer relay depth. A depth-\(H\) relay alphabet is a finite set \(\mathcal A_H\) with state count
\begin{equation}
z(H):=|\mathcal A_H|.
\end{equation}
Each state carries a signed relay-depth label. The neutral relay state has label \(0\); the two oriented branches have labels \(+h\) and \(-h\), \(h\geq 1\). A depth-\(H\) relay resolves all branch depths \(h=1,\ldots,H\). Thus an admissible relay alphabet must contain at least one neutral state and, for every represented nonzero depth, the corresponding reversed branch state. A nonzero state whose reversed partner is absent is an orphan state and is not closed under relay reversal.

\paragraph{A1 (relay-block additivity).}
Independent relay rungs compose by Cartesian product of their code books. For independent relay alphabets \(\mathcal A_{H_1},\ldots,\mathcal A_{H_m}\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_{H_1,\ldots,H_m}
=
\mathcal A_{H_1}\times\cdots\times \mathcal A_{H_m},
\qquad
|\mathcal A_{H_1,\ldots,H_m}|
=
\prod_{i=1}^m z(H_i),
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\ln |\mathcal A_{H_1,\ldots,H_m}|
=
\sum_{i=1}^m \ln z(H_i).
\end{equation}
The same additivity requires branch reversal closure: if a relay state of signed depth \(+h\) is admissible, then a state of signed depth \(-h\) is admissible, with \(0\) as the neutral identity.

\paragraph{A2 (code-volume monotonicity).}
The local state count is strictly increasing with relay depth:
\begin{equation}
H_2>H_1 \quad\Longrightarrow\quad z(H_2)>z(H_1).
\end{equation}

\paragraph{A3 (dimensional consistency).}
The local relay code volume is a count of states:
\begin{equation}
z(H)\in \mathbb Z_{\geq 0}
\qquad\text{for every }H\in\mathbb N.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{A4 (minimal integer extension).}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be the class of integer-valued relay state-count functions generated by admissible alphabet families satisfying A1--A3 and the unit-depth anchor
\begin{equation}
z(1)=3=2\cdot 1+1.
\end{equation}
The selected relay state count is the pointwise-minimal element of \(\mathcal C\):
\begin{equation}
z(H)=\min_{\widetilde z\in\mathcal C}\widetilde z(H)
\qquad
\text{for every }H\in\mathbb N.
\end{equation}
The anchor fixes the primitive depth-one relay alphabet, up to relabeling, as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_1=\{-1,0,+1\}.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Part 2. Lemma chain.}

\paragraph{Lemma 1 (product factorisation of independent relay volume).}
A1 and A3 imply that the cumulative code volume of an independent relay block factorises into integer rung factors. For an \(m\)-rung block,
\begin{equation}
Z(H_1,\ldots,H_m)
=
\prod_{i=1}^m z(H_i),
\qquad
\ln Z(H_1,\ldots,H_m)
=
\sum_{i=1}^m \ln z(H_i).
\end{equation}
For a homogeneous depth-\(H\) block with \(H\) independent relay calls to the same local alphabet,
\begin{equation}
Z_H=z(H)^H,
\qquad
\ln Z_H=H\ln z(H).
\end{equation}

\emph{Proof sketch.}
The Cartesian product rule in A1 gives the first identity by elementary cardinal arithmetic. A3 ensures that each factor is an integer state count. The object that factorises is the independent-block volume \(Z_H\), whereas \(z(H)\) is the local alphabet size selected by the minimality axiom.

\paragraph{Lemma 2 (paired-depth lower bound).}
Every admissible depth-\(H\) relay alphabet satisfying A1 contains at least \(2H+1\) distinct states:
\begin{equation}
z(H)\geq 2H+1.
\end{equation}

\emph{Proof sketch.}
Depth \(H\) means that the positive relay depths \(1,\ldots,H\) are resolved. For each \(h\in\{1,\ldots,H\}\), A1 requires both the \(+h\) branch state and the reversed \(-h\) branch state. These two states are distinct because \(h\neq -h\). A1 also requires a neutral identity state \(0\). Hence any admissible alphabet contains at least
\begin{equation}
\{-H,\ldots,-1,0,1,\ldots,H\},
\end{equation}
which has cardinality \(2H+1\). A2 is then automatically respected by the minimal paired extension, since each new relay depth adds a new pair of branch states.

\paragraph{Lemma 3 (ladder alphabet saturation).}
The signed alphabet
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_H:=\{-H,-H+1,\ldots,-1,0,1,\ldots,H-1,H\}
\end{equation}
is admissible under A1--A3, satisfies the anchor \(z(1)=3\), and attains the lower bound in Lemma 2:
\begin{equation}
|\mathcal K_H|=2H+1.
\end{equation}

\emph{Proof sketch.}
The alphabet \(\mathcal K_H\) contains exactly one neutral state and exactly one state for each oriented branch depth \(\pm h\), \(h=1,\ldots,H\). It is closed under branch reversal, contains no orphan symbol, and has integer cardinality. Its state count is strictly increasing:
\begin{equation}
|\mathcal K_{H+1}|-|\mathcal K_H|=2.
\end{equation}
At \(H=1\), \(\mathcal K_1=\{-1,0,+1\}\), so the anchor is reproduced exactly.

\paragraph{Lemma 4 (uniqueness of the minimal state count).}
A1--A4 uniquely select
\begin{equation}
z(H)=2H+1.
\end{equation}

\emph{Proof sketch.}
Lemma 2 gives the universal lower bound \(\widetilde z(H)\geq 2H+1\) for every admissible anchored integer state-count function \(\widetilde z\in\mathcal C\). Lemma 3 constructs an admissible alphabet attaining this bound for every \(H\). Therefore the pointwise minimum required by A4 is exactly \(2H+1\). Other alphabets may be isomorphic by relabeling, but the state-count formula is unique.

\paragraph{Lemma 5 (relay-cost calculus).}
With the relay-block log-volume from Lemma 1, the exponent displacement is
\begin{equation}
\epsilon(H)=\frac{1}{H\ln z(H)}.
\end{equation}
Substituting the A1--A4 state count gives
\begin{equation}
\epsilon(H)=\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)},
\end{equation}
and hence the two ladder branches are
\begin{equation}
\beta_\pm(H)
=
1\pm \epsilon(H)
=
1\pm \frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)}.
\end{equation}

\emph{Proof sketch.}
A homogeneous depth-\(H\) relay block has independent-block volume \(Z_H=z(H)^H\). Its log-volume is therefore \(H\ln z(H)\). Taking the reciprocal relay cost as the exponent displacement and inserting the unique minimal state count from Lemma 4 yields the stated closed form.

\paragraph{Part 3. Alternative formula axiom-violation table.}
For any proposed displacement \(f(H)\), comparison with the relay-cost identity
\begin{equation}
f(H)=\frac{1}{H\ln z(H)}
\end{equation}
implies the effective state count
\begin{equation}
z_f(H)=\exp\!\left(\frac{1}{Hf(H)}\right).
\end{equation}
The following table lists the induced state count and the corresponding axiom failure.

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.35}
\begin{tabular}{p{0.24\linewidth}p{0.28\linewidth}p{0.40\linewidth}}
\hline
Candidate displacement & Implied state count & Axiom status \\
\hline
\(\displaystyle \epsilon(H)=\frac{1}{H^2}\)
&
\(\displaystyle \ln z(H)=H,\quad z(H)=e^H\)
&
Violates A3: \(e^H\) is not an integer state count for integer \(H\geq 1\), and the anchor gives \(z(1)=e\neq 3\); A4 is therefore not reached. \\

\(\epsilon(H)=\tfrac{1}{H\ln(3H+1)}\)
&
\(z(H)=3H+1\)
&
Violates anchored A4: the formula gives \(z(1)=4\neq 3\), and even if the unit anchor is patched by hand, \(3H+1>2H+1\) adds redundant states beyond the minimal balanced relay alphabet. \\

\(\epsilon(H)=\tfrac{1}{H\ln(H+1)}\)
&
\(z(H)=H+1\)
&
Violates the anchor and relay-closure content of A1: \(z(1)=2\neq 3\), and \(H+1<2H+1\) cannot contain \(H\) positive branch states, their \(H\) reversed partners, and a neutral state. \\

\(\epsilon(H)=\tfrac{1}{H}\)
&
\(\ln z(H)=1,\quad z(H)=e\)
&
Violates A3 because \(e\) is not an integer count; it also fails A2 as a constant state count and misses the anchor \(z(1)=3\). \\

\(\epsilon(H)=\tfrac{1}{(2H+1)\ln(2H+1)}\)
&
\(\begin{aligned}
\ln z(H)&=\tfrac{2H+1}{H}\ln(2H+1),\\
z(H)&=(2H+1)^{(2H+1)/H}
\end{aligned}\)
&
Violates A3 for every integer \(H\geq 2\), since \((2H+1)^{1/H}\) is not an integer; at \(H=1\) it gives \(z(1)=27\neq 3\). If instead read as keeping \(z=2H+1\) but replacing the rung factor \(H\) by \(2H+1\), it violates A1 block additivity. \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{Part 4. Conclusion.}
The relay-depth formula is therefore the unique state-count formula consistent with A1--A4; the empirical near-equivalents are descriptive curve fits without axiomatic backing and are not falsifiable theories of urban scaling on the present axiom system.

% --- Cross-paper scope note (副 2): Paper 5 anti-falsification statement ---
\paragraph{Cross-paper scope note.}
The present paper's 22/22 closure is independent of and not validated by cross-time $\beta$ data. The post-1971 $\beta$ trajectory anchors (1900--04, 1940--60, 2021--25) discussed in Paper~5~\cite{Kato2026e} SI under a measurement-type-aware reconciliation lie outside the operational scope of the cross-sectional Bettencourt 22-panel test reported here. The 22/22 closure should therefore be read as a single-epoch cross-sectional structural calibration, not as a cross-time longitudinal validation; the cross-time falsification record is reported and adjudicated in Paper~5 and Paper~3 SI under their respective scope rules.

% --- CPC blind test CI disclosure (副 1) ---
\paragraph{CPC blind test CI disclosure.}
For the CPC blind-test sectors discussed at Table~2 of the main text, the per-sector observed exponent and the associated 95\,\% CI gap to the ladder prediction are: Tech (G+H): $\beta_{\rm obs}=1.289$, $|\Delta|=0.022$; Life (A): $\beta_{\rm obs}=1.220$, $|\Delta|=0.049$; Chem (C): $\beta_{\rm obs}=1.060$, $|\Delta|=0.111$; Mech (B): $\beta_{\rm obs}=1.042$, $|\Delta|=0.129$. The implied minimum half-width of the per-sector 95\,\% CI required to retain CI coverage at the ladder prediction is $\ge\!0.13$ for the Mech sector. The per-sector sample sizes $n_{\rm section}$ and the heteroscedasticity-robust standard errors backing these CIs are: Tech (G+H) $n\!=\!428$, SE\,$\approx\!0.040$; Life (A) $n\!=\!312$, SE\,$\approx\!0.052$; Chem (C) $n\!=\!269$, SE\,$\approx\!0.070$; Mech (B) $n\!=\!221$, SE\,$\approx\!0.075$. CI half-widths therefore scale approximately as $2\,\mathrm{SE}\!\in\![0.08,0.15]$, with Mech (B) at the upper end driven by sample-size attrition; the CPC blind test exit for Chem / Mech is therefore a CI-coverage closure rather than a tight central-value reproduction.



% V22.9 inc_03 P4b1_003 Heff sensitivity coordinate (paper4b_1 cycle 2 W1)
\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate. Tier B mixing-coordinate framing as ex post diagnostic}
\sloppy
\label{sec:S-Heff-sensitivity-coordinate}

\paragraph{1. Coordinate identity and degrees-of-freedom accounting.}
We state upfront that the construction below is presented as an \emph{ex post} mixing-coordinate diagnostic on the fixed integer ladder, not as an independent predictive closure of the Tier B exponents. The predictive content of the framework rests on the seventeen Tier A rows, whose integer rungs are assigned from network observables (network type, substrate constraint, branch sign) without consulting the empirical exponent. The five Tier B rows are flagged as hybrid rows pending independent network-feature verification by a separate \(\beta_{\rm obs}\)-blind procedure (forthcoming work). For a Tier B row the branch sign is fixed by whether the empirical exponent is superlinear or sublinear. With
\[
\varepsilon(H)=\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)},
\]
the reported continuous coordinate satisfies
\[
\beta_{\rm pred}
=
\beta_\pm(H_{\rm eff})
=
1\pm \varepsilon(H_{\rm eff}),
\qquad
H_{\rm eff}:=\varepsilon^{-1}\!\left(|\beta_{\rm obs}-1|\right).
\]
Thus, after the sign has been assigned, \(\beta_{\rm pred}=\beta_{\rm obs}\) by definition whenever the inverse exists on the admissible range. A confidence-interval overlap in these rows is therefore not an independent predictive test of the exponent value. On its face, the display above could be read as a one-parameter rowwise fit, with one continuous degree of freedom assigned to each Tier B row. Under that naive accounting the five Tier B rows would carry five row-specific exponent degrees of freedom.

The accounting used here is stricter. The exponent curve \(\beta_\pm(H)\) is not adjusted in Tier B: it is the same ladder used in the direct-strict rows. The continuous number \(H_{\rm eff}\) is reported as a coordinate reading on that already specified ladder. Consequently the Tier B rows are not included as direct exponent predictions. They are closure rows: they ask where a composite observable falls along the integer relay-depth ladder once its empirical exponent has been measured.

\paragraph{2. Reinterpretation as a measurement on a discrete ladder.}
The relay-depth model supplies a discrete set of pure rungs \(H\in\mathbb{Z}_{\geq 1}\), with departures from linearity given by \(\varepsilon(H)\). A composite observable is admissible only as a convex mixture of integer-rung contributions,
\[
|\beta_{\rm obs}-1|
=
\varepsilon(H_{\rm eff})
=
\sum_k \lambda_k\,\varepsilon(H_k),
\qquad
\sum_k \lambda_k=1,\quad \lambda_k\geq 0,\quad H_k\in\mathbb{Z}_{\geq 1}.
\]
Equivalently, since \(\varepsilon(H)\) is monotone on the relevant domain, the observed departure has a unique coordinate \(H_{\rm eff}\) whenever it lies in the ladder range.

For a named adjacent pair \(\{H_a,H_b\}\), \(H_a<H_b\), the coordinate is one-dimensional. If the mixture is expressed in the exponent-displacement coordinate, the barycentric weight is
\[
\lambda_a
=
\frac{\varepsilon(H_{\rm eff})-\varepsilon(H_b)}
     {\varepsilon(H_a)-\varepsilon(H_b)},
\qquad
\lambda_b=1-\lambda_a .
\]
If the mixture is expressed in the relay-depth coordinate, the reported weight is instead
\[
H_{\rm eff}=\pi_a H_a+(1-\pi_a)H_b,
\qquad
\pi_a=\frac{H_b-H_{\rm eff}}{H_b-H_a},
\qquad
\pi_b=1-\pi_a .
\]
These two coordinate systems are deterministically related once the integer pair is fixed. Jensen convexity of \(\varepsilon(H)\) supplies the known curvature between the depth-coordinate mixture and the exponent-coordinate mixture; it does not introduce an additional exponent parameter.

Thus \(H_{\rm eff}\) carries the same information as a single mixing weight \(\pi\in[0,1]\) after the discrete pair has been specified. The Tier B rows therefore add five mixing-coordinate readings on the fixed integer ladder. They do not add five fitted exponent parameters. The exponent-parameter count remains zero; the mixing-coordinate count is five.

\paragraph{2'. Pending independent network-feature verification.}
The mixing-coordinate count of five reported here is a diagnostic readout, not yet an independent derivation. A separate \(\beta_{\rm obs}\)-blind verification procedure, in which mixture weights \(\pi\) for each Tier B row are obtained from network-feature inputs (degree distribution, modularity, path-length statistics, substrate-resource bound, branch sign, and observation-derived \(H_{\max}\)) by a pre-registered replicator-dynamics simulation, is currently under construction and will be reported in a follow-up paper. Until that verification is complete, the present Tier B section is to be read as an \emph{ex post} ladder-coordinate audit: it documents that the five hybrid panels are admissible on the pre-specified \(H=\{2,3\}\) cell, but it does not stand as a parameter-free derivation of their exponents. Readers who require a strictly network-derived test of Tier B closures should restrict the panel scoring to the seventeen Tier A rows.

\paragraph{2''. Universal \(\beta\) predictor companion tool.}
A companion browser-based simulator implementing the registered consistency rule is publicly available at \url{https://aiandfuture.co.jp/tool/8/}. The tool presents the 22-indicator Bettencourt panel as a clickable reference catalogue, displays the analytical \(\beta_{\pm}(H)\) at the structurally-assigned integer rung for each indicator (per V261 SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins}), and includes a live in-browser cluster-analysis demonstration on real coordination-network data (USPTO 2010 assignee-level co-inventorship for the patents rows) using a graph-shape \(K\) detection rule (modularity at forced \(K{=}2\) satisfying \(Q_{K=2}\ge 0.20\), a criterion independent of \(\beta_{\rm obs}\)). The 22/22 closure claim of the present paper rests on the match between real empirical \(\beta_{\rm obs}\) from independent panel data sources (USPTO PatentsView for patents, OECD MSA for GDP, BLS QCEW for wages, EIA state-level data for electricity, FDIC SOD for bank deposits, and so on as catalogued in SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins}) and the analytical formula \(\beta_{\pm}(H)=1\pm 1/[H\ln(2H+1)]\) at structurally-assigned \(H\); it does not rest on synthetic edgelist reconstruction. The tool itself uses zero fitted exponents and is offered as a reproducibility-and-demonstration instrument rather than as an external validator of the present panel. A first instance of the predictive Phase~B graph-derived verification has been carried out on the USPTO 2010 assignee-level co-inventorship network (\(n=3{,}951\) assignees, \(m=4{,}526\) edges): graph-shape \(K{=}2\) is detected (\(Q_{K=2}\ge 0.20\), independent of \(\beta_{\rm obs}\)), the graph-derived mixture weights are \(\pi_{\rm low}=0.943,\ \pi_{\rm up}=0.057\), yielding \(H_{\rm eff}=2.057\) and \(\beta_{\rm pred}=1.298\), against the row-17 observed \(\beta_{\rm obs}=1.298\,[1.198,1.398]\). The graph-derived stage (\(K\) detection plus the mixture weights \((\pi_{\rm low},\pi_{\rm up})\)) is thus instantiated for the patents rows with zero fitted exponents; the underlying integer \(H\)-pair itself remains a structural input per V261 SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins} author assignment, with formal graph-property-to-\(H\) derivation reserved as open future work.

\paragraph{3. Tier B coordinate readings.}
All five Tier B rows fall in the same adjacent two-rung cell, \(H\in\{2,3\}\), with the gasoline rows on the sublinear mirror branch and the AIDS/inventor/patent rows on the superlinear branch. For this cell,
\[
\pi_2=3-H_{\rm eff},\qquad \pi_3=H_{\rm eff}-2 .
\]
Rounded coordinate readings are:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.16\linewidth}p{0.09\linewidth}p{0.07\linewidth}p{0.06\linewidth}p{0.06\linewidth}p{0.13\linewidth}p{0.20\linewidth}}
\hline
Tier B row & Branch & Integer cell & \(H_{\rm eff}\) & \(\beta_{\rm pred}\) & \(\beta_{\rm obs}\) [95\,\% CI] & Mixing-coordinate reading \\
\hline
Gasoline sales & sublinear & \(\{2,3\}\) & \(\approx 2.61\) & 0.790 & \makecell[ct]{0.79 \\ {[0.73, 0.80]}} &
\(\pi_2\approx 0.39,\ \pi_3\approx 0.61\) \\
Gasoline stations & sublinear & \(\{2,3\}\) & \(\approx 2.61\) & 0.790 & \makecell[ct]{0.77 \\ {[0.74, 0.81]}} &
\(\pi_2\approx 0.39,\ \pi_3\approx 0.61\) \\
AIDS deaths & superlinear & \(\{2,3\}\) & \(\approx 2.45\) & 1.230 & \makecell[ct]{1.23 \\ {[1.18, 1.29]}} &
\(\pi_2\approx 0.55,\ \pi_3\approx 0.45\) \\
Inventors & superlinear & \(\{2,3\}\) & \(\approx 2.32\) & 1.250 & \makecell[ct]{1.25 \\ {[1.22, 1.27]}} &
\(\pi_2\approx 0.68,\ \pi_3\approx 0.32\) \\
Patents-legacy & superlinear & \(\{2,3\}\) & \(\approx 2.10\) & 1.289 & 1.27 [1.25, 1.29] &
\(\pi_2\approx 0.90,\ \pi_3\approx 0.10\) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The empirical content of Tier B is therefore not that five arbitrary exponents can be reproduced. The content is that five composite indicators map into the same pre-specified \(H=\{2,3\}\) cluster, or its sublinear mirror, with interpretable barycentric weights. The two gasoline rows read essentially the same coordinate. The three superlinear rows read coordinates just above the \(H=2\) rung, moving toward \(H=3\) in the order patents-legacy, inventors, AIDS deaths.

\paragraph{4. Falsifiability of the coordinate reading.}
A Tier B row is admissible only if its observed exponent lies inside the convex hull of its stated integer support. For an adjacent pair \(H_a<H_b\), this condition is
\[
|\beta_{\rm obs}-1|\in
\left[\varepsilon(H_b),\varepsilon(H_a)\right].
\]
For the superlinear \(\{2,3\}\) cell this is
\[
\beta_{\rm obs}\in
[\beta_+(3),\beta_+(2)]
\approx
[1.171,1.311],
\]
and for the sublinear mirror cell this is
\[
\beta_{\rm obs}\in
[\beta_-(2),\beta_-(3)]
\approx
[0.689,0.829].
\]
If a superlinear Tier B row required \(\beta_{\rm obs}>\beta_+(2)=1.311\), then its coordinate would lie below \(H=2\) and it could not be accommodated in the stated \(\{2,3\}\) relay cell. Likewise, under a stated admissible band \(2\leq H\leq 8\), a superlinear row with \(\beta_{\rm obs}<\beta_+(8)\approx 1.044\) would require \(H_{\rm eff}>8\) and would fall outside the announced ladder band. In such a case the relay-depth account would fail for that row. The present five Tier B rows all lie inside the \(H=\{2,3\}\) convex hull, so their coordinate readings are well-defined.

\paragraph{5. Replacement sentence for the manuscript.}
The sentence ``\(H_{\rm eff}\) is reported only as a sensitivity coordinate'' should be replaced by the stronger accounting statement:
\begin{quote}
\itshape
For each Tier B row, \(H_{\rm eff}\) is the mixing-coordinate reading of the pre-specified integer pair \(\{H_a,H_b\}\); the row contains no fitted exponent parameter, only the single mixing-weight measurement \(\pi_a=(H_b-H_{\rm eff})/(H_b-H_a)\) with \(\pi_b=1-\pi_a\) on the fixed the ladder.
\end{quote}
Thus the Tier B accounting is explicit: exponent-parameter count \(=0\); mixing-coordinate count \(=5\).



% V23.0 inc_04 P4b1_004 data availability transparency (paper4b_1 cycle 2 W2)
\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-data-availability-disclosure. Frozen data assets, code release, and 30-day data-freeze plan}\label{sec:S-data-availability-disclosure}
\sloppy

\paragraph{Part 1. Frozen data assets: public reproducibility status.}
This subsection distinguishes two notions of reproducibility. First, the empirical quantities used in the analysis are reproducible from publicly available sources using the definitions and estimation procedures stated in the main text and SI. Second, a frozen processed-data companion fixes the exact row-level values used by the scripts and tables. The latter is a convenience and verification layer, not a substitute for the public source provenance.

\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Bettencourt 22-panel.} The 22-indicator urban-scaling panel is derived from the public supplementary table of Bettencourt et al. (2007), \emph{PNAS}, DOI \href{https://doi.org/10.1073/pnas.0610172104}{10.1073/pnas.0610172104}; the supporting information is available at \url{https://www.pnas.org/doi/suppl/10.1073/pnas.0610172104}. The paper uses the reported exponent estimates and native uncertainty intervals for the corresponding indicator rows, together with the regime labels and ladder-comparison quantities defined in the present manuscript.

    \item \textbf{USPTO--CBSA patent panel, 2001 and 2010 anchors.} The patent-anchor estimates are reproducible from PatentsView bulk data tables, available at \url{https://s3.amazonaws.com/data.patentsview.org/download/}, and U.S. Census Bureau metropolitan population data from the Population Estimates Program, \url{https://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/popest.html}. The processed beta exponents for the 2001 and 2010 windows are derivable from these two public sources by the CBSA assignment, population matching, windowing, and log--log estimation procedure specified in main-text \S\ref{subsec:patent_anchor}. The present release does not yet provide the USPTO--CBSA processed panel as a single download.

    \item \textbf{BEA GDP-by-industry tables.} The GDP sector-composition inputs used for the sectoral composition and effective-depth identification are public BEA GDP-by-industry tables, available at \url{https://www.bea.gov/data/gdp/gdp-industry}. These tables enter the analysis as sectoral weights and sector-composition summaries; no fitted continuous exponent parameter is introduced in the Tier-B effective-depth sensitivity calculation.

    \item \textbf{CPC patent-classification panel.} The CPC-based patent panel is reproducible from the same PatentsView bulk data source, filtered by CPC group, together with the public Cooperative Patent Classification scheme files and definitions, available through the CPC portal at \url{https://www.cooperativepatentclassification.org/cpcSchemeAndDefinitions/table}, with classification resources also linked through WIPO at \url{https://www.wipo.int/classifications/}. The CPC panel is used only after applying the pre-specified CPC grouping and filtering rules described in the manuscript and SI.

    \item \textbf{EOC bootstrap inputs.} The Era-of-Crystallisation bootstrap uses interval summaries rather than private microdata. Its inputs consist of: (i) the native Bettencourt et al. exponent intervals for the 22-panel rows; (ii) patent-anchor intervals generated from the public USPTO--CBSA pipeline; (iii) CPC group-level patent intervals generated from the public CPC-filtered PatentsView pipeline; (iv) BEA sector-composition weights and the associated effective-depth bands used in the sectoral diagnostic; and (v) auxiliary indicator-specific ``aux-band'' intervals cited in the SI wherever an uncertainty band is not taken directly from the Bettencourt supplementary table. The frozen data companion will record, for each bootstrap row, the point estimate, lower and upper bounds, interval type, regime label, and reference source.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Part 2. Code release status.}
The repository \url{https://github.com/shota-kato-lab/kato-equation-paper4} at tag \texttt{v1.4} contains the LaTeX source for the manuscript and SI and the scripts required to reproduce the numerical closure checks reported in the paper. In particular, the release includes \texttt{scripts/sim\_paper4\_22\_22\_full\_impl\_v4.py}, which implements ladder closure, the alternative-formula comparison, and the Panel-A 22-row blind scan; \texttt{scripts/poisson\_binomial\_random\_H.py}, which implements the Poisson-binomial dynamic program under the three operational definitions used in the SI; and \texttt{scripts/paper4\_mae\_rmse\_canonical.py}, which consolidates the three-tier MAE/RMSE calculations. The repository also contains \texttt{KNOWN\_ISSUES.md}, the five-issue self-disclosure file integrated into the SI as \S\ref{sec:S-KNOWN-ISSUES-integrated}. The Zenodo deposit, DOI \href{https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.20145298}{10.5281/zenodo.20145298}, at \texttt{v1.4} contains the same release materials together with the LaTeX-compiled PDF.

\paragraph{Part 3. Thirty-day processed-data freeze plan.}
Within 30 days of \texttt{v1.4} acceptance or public arXiv release, whichever occurs first, a processed-data companion will be added to the Zenodo record as \texttt{v1.4.1}, with no change to the manuscript text. This companion will include one CSV file for the 22-panel closure analysis containing the exact \(\beta_{\rm obs}\), lower and upper interval bounds, regime label, ladder target, residual quantity, and reference source for each row used in the paper. The same release will include a README specifying column definitions, source provenance, and checksum information.

The USPTO--CBSA per-MSA, per-year processed patent panel for the 2001 and 2010 anchors will likewise be deposited as \texttt{v1.4.1}, or as \texttt{v1.4.2} if it is packaged separately. This file will contain the processed MSA identifiers, year, patent counts under the stated counting rule, matched CBSA population, and the anchor-window variables required to reproduce the reported patent-scaling estimates. The phrase ``available from the corresponding author on request'' in the Data and Code Availability statement is therefore a temporary stop-gap during the initial \texttt{v1.4} release window. It is not intended as a permanent restriction on the processed panel data underlying the reported numerical results.

\paragraph{Part 4. Rationale for the staged deposit.}
The \texttt{v1.4} release prioritised manuscript-level integrity and numerical reproducibility: five independent-review findings were addressed in the text, SI, and computational scripts, including the alignment of reported numerical values with the analytical ladder implementation. Packaging the processed tabular data was scoped as a follow-on deposit because the underlying quantities are reproducible from public sources using the methods stated in the paper. A frozen CSV companion nevertheless provides a stronger open-science verification layer by fixing the exact row-level values used in the closure analysis, patent anchors, and bootstrap inputs. For that reason, the processed data will be deposited on the 30-day schedule specified above.

\clearpage
\section*{SI Appendix S-path1-microfoundation. Cross-branch cancellation microfoundation for the five balanced indicators and Bridge to Paper~3 \(H_{\rm obs}\) theory}\label{sec:S-path1-microfoundation}
\sloppy

\subsection*{Part 1. Setup}

At relay depth \(H\), the rung has signed alphabet
\[
\mathcal{A}_H=\{-H,\ldots,-1,0,+1,\ldots,+H\},\qquad |\mathcal{A}_H|=2H+1 .
\]
Positive symbols represent growth or aggregating channels: co-location, matching, specialization, or interaction-driven outputs whose marginal contribution increases with urban density. Negative symbols represent constraint or dissipative channels: geometric coverage, congestion, replacement, maintenance, or bounded-infrastructure effects whose marginal contribution is reduced by urban scale. The neutral symbol \(0\) carries the baseline linear demographic channel.

Let \(p_H(a)\) be the probability mass assigned to symbol \(a\in\mathcal{A}_H\). Define
\[
\pi_+ = \sum_{a=1}^{H} p_H(a),\qquad
\pi_- = \sum_{a=-H}^{-1} p_H(a),\qquad
\sigma_{\rm gc}=\pi_+-\pi_- .
\]
Here \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\) is the generation--coverage asymmetry of the relay block. Pure positive polarity has \(\sigma_{\rm gc}=+1\), pure negative polarity has \(\sigma_{\rm gc}=-1\), and a balanced signed block has \(\sigma_{\rm gc}=0\). Neutral mass \(p_H(0)\) is allowed and does not affect the signed asymmetry.

The increment $\varepsilon(H)$ is
\[
\epsilon(H)=\frac{1}{H\ln(2H+1)},\qquad
\beta_\pm(H)=1\pm \epsilon(H).
\]
For a relay block with signed mixture \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\), the effective exponent is
\[
\beta_{\rm eff}(H)=1+\sigma_{\rm gc}\,\epsilon(H).
\]
Thus a balanced block with \(\pi_+=\pi_-\) gives
\[
\sigma_{\rm gc}=0\quad\Longrightarrow\quad \beta_{\rm eff}=1
\]
independently of \(H\). Path--1 rows are therefore not assigned linearity by choosing a special rung. They are assigned linearity because the signed relay flux cancels before the rung increment is expressed.

\subsection*{Part 2. Microfoundation for the five Path--1 indicators}

The common structure of the five balanced indicators is that their natural unit is an accounting stock or saturated per-capita service tied to persons, households, or operating units. Write such a quantity as
\[
X(N)=N\,x(N),\qquad \beta_X=1+\frac{d\ln x}{d\ln N}.
\]
Path--1 corresponds to a stable urban regime in which feedbacks keep \(x(N)\) approximately constant across the metropolitan scaling window. In relay language, the positive branch that would raise \(x\) is offset by the negative branch that would lower \(x\), giving \(\pi_+=\pi_-\) and hence \(\sigma_{\rm gc}=0\).

\paragraph{Housing units.}
Housing units are a stock whose primary function is to house resident households. The positive branch is new construction, subdivision, conversion, and densification following population growth. The negative branch is demolition, depreciation, vacancy, affordability pressure, land-use limits, and removal of obsolete stock. In steady-state urban dynamics, the stock is regulated by vacancy rates, household formation, rents, credit conditions, and planning constraints. If housing units per resident household fall too low, prices and crowding induce construction or conversion; if they rise too high, vacancies, disinvestment, and demolition increase. These feedbacks stabilize the housing-unit-to-population ratio, so the growth flux and the replacement/constraint flux balance at the exponent level. The resulting relay block has \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\simeq 0\), giving \(\beta\simeq 1\).

\paragraph{Households.}
Households are the occupied counterpart of housing units and inherit the same Path--1 mechanism. The positive branch is household formation: migration, family splitting, young-adult independence, and creation of new occupied units as the city grows. The negative branch is co-residence, delayed household formation, crowding, cost pressure, and demographic composition effects that reduce households per capita. In mature metropolitan systems, average household size varies slowly relative to total population. The household count is therefore approximately \(N\) divided by a stable household-size factor. The positive formation channel and the negative co-residence/cost channel cancel in the signed relay mass, so households are treated as the proxy-balanced version of housing.

\paragraph{Household water.}
Household water consumption is a saturated per-capita service. The positive branch consists of universal connection, indoor plumbing, appliances, convenience use, outdoor watering, and income-linked comfort demand. The negative branch consists of metering, tiered pricing, leak control, low-flow fixtures, drought restrictions, conservation norms, and infrastructure efficiency. Once household water service is near universal, biological and hygiene requirements impose a natural per-capita scale, while utility management and price feedbacks suppress unbounded growth in use per person. Larger cities may provide more convenience and higher service reliability, but they also tend to have stronger conservation, metering, and infrastructure management. These opposing signed channels make household water a balanced service to first order, with \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\simeq 0\) and \(\beta\simeq 1\).

\paragraph{Employment.}
Employment is bounded by the resident population through labor-force participation, age structure, unemployment, commuting capture, and retirement. The positive branch is labor-market deepening: thicker matching, more job categories, higher participation opportunities, and improved employment search in large cities. The negative branch is the out-of-labor-force population, students, retirees, disability, unemployment, household specialization, and residential sorting. In developed-economy metropolitan systems, the employment-to-population ratio is a slowly varying demographic-institutional quantity rather than an unbounded interaction output. Urban scale changes wages and productivity more strongly than it changes the fraction of persons counted as employed. The signed relay contributions therefore balance near the extensive baseline, giving \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\simeq 0\).

\paragraph{Establishments.}
Establishments are operating units, not value added. The positive branch is entry: new firms, branches, service outlets, and niche establishments enabled by larger local markets. The negative branch is exit, consolidation, larger average establishment size, rent pressure, competition, franchising scale economies, and merger of functions into fewer units. A larger city supports more varieties of establishments, but it also supports larger establishments and more intense competition. Entry and exit are coupled by market-clearing and profit conditions, so the number of establishments per capita is stabilized more strongly than output per establishment. This makes establishments structurally analogous to housing units: a stock of operating containers whose count tracks population, while intensive economic value is expressed elsewhere. Hence establishments are placed on Path--1 as a structural balanced row.

\subsection*{Part 3. Why GDP, wages, and electricity are not balanced}

GDP, wages, and electricity do not share the same accounting constraint. Their per-capita intensities can rise with city size:
\[
Y(N)=N\,y(N),\qquad \frac{d\ln y}{d\ln N}>0 .
\]
For GDP, the positive branch includes specialization, high-end services, financial flows, management functions, innovation, and interaction-driven matching. These are precisely the density mechanisms of classical urban scaling: larger cities do not merely contain more workers; they alter the value produced per worker.

Wages inherit the same positive asymmetry through the urban productivity premium. The wage variable is not a count of employed persons; it is an intensive payment per worker or aggregate labor income channel. Labor-market depth, skill sorting, knowledge spillovers, and firm-worker matching push the positive branch above the offsetting constraints.

Electricity is also not purely household service consumption at the metropolitan scale. Residential electricity is closer to a saturated per-capita component, but commercial and industrial demand form the larger signed contribution in the studied aggregate. Offices, dense commercial districts, elevators, cooling loads, data and communications infrastructure, hospitals, universities, and industrial activity couple electricity use to the superlinear economic functions of the city. The constraint branch is present, but it does not cancel the positive branch.

Thus these indicators have \(\sigma_{\rm gc}>0\), and in the direct integer-ladder classification their resolved polarity is positive. They are therefore assigned to the \(+\) branch, \(\beta_+(H)\), for the appropriate relay depth \(H\in\{4,5,6\}\), rather than to the Path--1 balanced class.

\subsection*{Part 4. Falsifiability of \(\sigma_{\rm gc}=0\)}

Path--1 makes a sharp prediction:
\[
\sigma_{\rm gc}=0\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad \beta=1 .
\]
Because this prediction is independent of \(H\), it is directly falsifiable. If any Path--1 indicator is estimated with high statistical confidence to have \(\beta\neq 1\), for example if a bootstrap confidence interval excludes \(1\), then the balanced relay assumption is broken for that indicator. The row should then be removed from Path--1 and reclassified by the sign and magnitude of its deviation onto the appropriate integer \(+\) or \(-\) branch.

The present five Path--1 rows pass this check. Housing units are centered at \(\beta\simeq 1.000\) with interval including \(1\); household water and employment have point estimates near \(1.010\) with intervals including \(1\); households are the proxy counterpart of housing; and establishments are retained as the structural operating-unit analogue. The available point estimates or structural anchors are therefore at the \(\pm 0.01\)--\(0.02\) level around unity, with no reported high-confidence exclusion of \(\beta=1\).

\subsection*{Part 5. Bridge to Paper~3 \(H_{\rm obs}\) theory}

Paper~3 gives the upstream \(H_{\rm obs}\) account of when \(\sigma_{\rm gc}\to 0\) emerges: steady-state institutional saturation creates a balanced generation--coverage fixed point. The full derivation belongs to the Paper~3 SI and is not repeated here.

% --- end of S-path1-microfoundation ---

\bigskip
\section*{Companion simulator}
An interactive browser-based companion simulator for the analyses in this paper is publicly available at \url{https://aiandfuture.co.jp/tool/8/}. The simulator presents all 22 Bettencourt 2007 indicators with the analytical \(\beta_{\pm}(H)\) ladder predictions per V261 SI~\textsf{S-PanelOrigins} and includes a live in-browser cluster analysis on real coordination-network data (USPTO 2010 assignee-level co-inventorship for the patents rows), using a graph-shape \(K\) detection rule independent of \(\beta_{\rm obs}\).
